> A: This is so unfair. That was my wedding gift!
> C: Lin, if you ever get married, I'll give it to you.
> B: Don't worry, that will never happen.
> C: I know. Does anyone want tea?

## 148. Pirates Are Cool

> Zari and Junior are at an amusement park.
> A: Thanks for bringing me to Pirate Land, Zari! Everything here is so cool!
> B: Yeah, I used to love this place when I was your age.
> A: Let's go see the singing pirate show!
> B: No, they're terrible singers.
> A: Well, then can you buy me a pirate hat?
> B: Sorry, your dad only gave us money for food and rides.
> Suddenly, Zari sees a boy from school.
> B: Oh no! It's Paul!
> B: I don't want him to see me here! I really like him! He'll think I'm not cool!
> A: But Pirate Land is super cool!
> B: Let's hide in the gift shop.
> They run into the gift shop.
> A: I have an idea. You can wear a pirate costume! Then Paul won't know who you are!
> B: I don't know…
> A: Put on this hat, this eye patch… and this fake beard!
> B: Junior, this is crazy!
> A: Look, Paul is coming over here!
> B: Ugh! Fine!
> Zari quickly buys and puts on the costume.
> Paul sees Zari.
> C: Zari, is that you?
> B: Um… hi, Paul.
> C: Wow, you really like pirates, don't you?
> B: Haha… No. I hate pirates!
> C: But you're wearing a pirate costume.
> B: Uh… yeah… The kid I'm babysitting loves pirates.
> C: Well, I think pirates are cool. I'm actually performing in the singing pirate show.
> B: What?!
> C: I was going to invite you, but you just said you hate pirates…
> B: Wait, I actually love pirates! I was joking!
> C: I have to go.
> Paul walks away.
> A: Sorry, Zari. Can I have your pirate hat?

## 149. The Magic School

> Eddy is in the kitchen reading his son Junior's book.
> A: Is that my book about the boy who goes to the magic school?
> B: Yes! This book is so good! I can't wait to see how it ends.
> A: Well, Peter fights the evil snake king…
> B: Stop! Don't tell me!
> A: Hmmm…
> Junior opens the freezer.
> A: If I can have ice cream before dinner, then I won't tell you how the book ends.
> B: What? No!
> A: OK. Then the book ends when Peter runs into the dark forest…
> B: Wait! You can have ice cream before dinner. But only tonight!
> A: Yay! I'm going to eat it while I watch that new movie, 101 Murders.
> B: No, that movie is too scary for you!
> A: If you don't let me watch it, then I'll tell you how the book ends…
> B: Junior…
> A: …so Peter and his friends find the snake king's palace…
> B: OK! You can watch the movie.
> B: Just don't tell me the ending of this book.
> Later that week, Eddy is in the kitchen making dinner.
> Junior goes to the freezer to get some ice cream.
> B: Sorry, Junior.
> B: You can't have ice cream tonight.
> A: OK… So then I have to tell you how the book ends…
> B: You're too late! I already finished the book, so I know what happens!
> A: Oh no.
> B: And I read the rest of the books in the series!
> A: What?!
> B: Now you have to clean your room, or I'll tell you what happens in the next three books!

## 150. I Love Boxing

> Lin and Oscar are in a coffee shop.
> Oscar is telling Lin a story when he notices that she's asleep.
> A: Lin, are you asleep?
> B: What? Oh… Sorry. I've been very tired lately.
> A: Oh, I know what will help you.
> B: What?
> A: I just started boxing classes!
> A: You should come with me tomorrow. I promise, it will give you more energy.
> The next day, Lin meets Oscar outside his boxing class.
> Oscar is wearing shorts and boxing gloves.
> B: Wow, you have your own boxing gloves?
> A: Of course! I'm a real boxer! Now let's go inside.
> Later, Lin is in the class. She looks tired. The teacher walks over to her.
> C: Are you OK?
> B: No, I'm extremely tired. I don't have any more energy.
> C: Are you new to this class?
> B: Yeah, Oscar invited me.
> C: Who's Oscar?
> B: That man over there.
> Lin looks around the room. Oscar is gone.
> Lin finds Oscar drinking a smoothie at the store next to the gym.
> B: Oscar, what are you doing?
> A: After class, I always get a smoothie.
> B: But you didn't finish the class.
> A: I finished half of it. I'll do the whole class next time. That was only my third class.
> B: You've only been to three boxing classes?
> A: Yeah, the class is OK, but this smoothie has changed my life! Here, taste it.
> Lin drinks some of the smoothie.
> B: Wow, how much sugar is in this?
> A: Two hundred grams. And as much caffeine as three cups of coffee!
> A: Don't you feel great?!
> B: Yeah, I love boxing!

## 151. An Old Friend

> Eddy is picking up Junior from school.
> A: Dad! Can we go to the park today? I want to play with Rusty.
> B: Absolutely! I like Rusty.
> B: He reminds me of my best friend when I was your age
> B: His name was Joe.
> B: We used to throw rocks into the lake, run around the neighborhood, and climb tall trees.
> A: That sounds like so much fun!
> B: But I haven't seen him since we were ten.
> B: I'm glad you have a friend like I had.
> Later that day, Eddy takes Junior to the park to see Rusty and his dad.
> C: Hi, I'm Rusty's dad. Wait, is that you, Eddy?!
> B: Joe?! I haven't seen you in such a long time!
> C: I can't believe it's you!
> Eddy and Joe hug.
> B: We used to have so much fun when we were kids!
> C: Yeah! We used to throw rocks in the lake to scare the ducks…
> B: Wait, what?
> C: Yeah! Stupid ducks.
> C: Remember when I broke your neighbor's window and we had to run from his dogs?
> B: Oh, that's right…
> C: And remember that time we were climbing a tree, and then I pushed you and you fell?
> B: I broke my leg!
> C: And you missed your big football game! Hahaha!
> B: I forgot about that.
> C: It's funny, your parents wouldn't let me hang out with you anymore after that.
> Eddy waves to Junior.
> B: Junior! It's time to go home.
> Eddy grabs Junior, and they leave.
> A: Dad, what's wrong? Why are we leaving?
> B: I don't want you to play with Rusty anymore.
> B: He reminds me of his dad.

## 152. Be Honest

> Oscar and his friend Lucy are at a fancy restaurant.
> A: The chef is my friend. He went to school in Paris to study cooking.
> B: I don't care where he went to school. I just want to eat!
> A waiter brings them plates of food.
> B: This looks great!
> A: But it smells strange.
> They start to eat. Suddenly, Oscar stops eating.
> A: The salmon is very salty…
> B: And the broccoli is too soft.
> A: And the shrimp is not cooked well.
> B: Oscar, this meal is awful.
> A: Ugh, you're right. But I can't be honest with him.
> A: He was so excited to open this restaurant.
> B: If you're really friends with him, then you need to be honest, Oscar.
> The chef comes to their table.
> C: Oscar, I'm glad you came! Do you like the food? It's my newest recipe!
> A: It's… well…
> A: I'm sorry. I have to be honest.
> A: The salmon… It's a little salty… and the broccoli, well…
> B: He means the food is bad. Sorry.
> C: Oh no. I was afraid it wasn't good. Thanks for being honest.
> C: You are a true friend.
> A: I am always happy to help.
> C: Then you both should come to my next dinner.
> C: You have to try the rest of my new recipes!
> Oscar and Lucy look at each other.
> B: Unfortunately, I'm leaving for a long vacation soon.
> A: You are?
> A: I mean, that's right, we're going together! We won't be back for many months.
> C: Really? When are you leaving?
> A: Uhh… Friday.
> C: Great! The dinner is tomorrow. You can still come!

## 153. At the Gym

> Eddy is at the gym exercising with his friend Bea.
> He sees a woman walk in with a handsome man.
> A: Oh no! I think my ex-girlfriend Penelope is here with her new boyfriend.
> B: Wow! He has a great body!
> A: Ugh, that doesn't make me feel better.
> B: I can't believe she brought him here. She knows you come to this gym every day!
> A: I need to start running. That'll make me feel better.
> Eddy walks over to the treadmill.
> The handsome man gets on the treadmill next to Eddy. He looks over at Eddy.
> C: Hi, do I know you?
> A: Sorry, I can't talk when I'm running.
> Eddy starts running on the treadmill.
> C: Wow, you're fast!
> A: I know!
> The handsome man starts to run.
> C: You're almost as fast as me!
> Eddy sees Penelope watching them from across the room.
> A: Actually, I can run faster than you!
> Eddy increases the speed on his treadmill.
> C: Is this a race? Because I love races!
> The handsome man increases his speed, too.
> C: Wait! I do know you. You dated Penelope!
> A: Penelope told you about me?!
> C: No, but I saw photos of you on her social media.
> Suddenly, Eddy falls off the treadmill. The handsome man stops running and helps him.
> Penelope runs over to Eddy.
> D: Are you OK?
> A: Not really. I just fell down in front of my ex-girlfriend and her new boyfriend!
> D: Boyfriend? No, this is Adam. He's my cousin!
> C: And I don't date women!
> A: Oh…
> C: Actually, I thought you were handsome.
> C: That's why I got on the treadmill next to you.

## 154. The Pie Festival

> Lucy and Vikram are at the pie festival. They each made a pie for a contest.
> They see Lin at the judge's table.
> A: Lin, I can't wait for you to taste my strawberry pie. Then you can tell everyone that it is the best!
> B: No, my apple pie is the best!
> C: I'll taste both pies and decide!
> B: Try mine first. I've been working on my recipes for years. I'm the best baker in town.
> A: You're wrong! Everyone knows that grandmothers make the best pies.
> Lin tries a slice of Vikram's pie.
> C: Wow… you're right. It's perfect.
> A: Now try mine!
> Lin eats a slice of Lucy's pie.
> C: Yours is also great, Grandma! It's sweet but not too sweet!
> B: But which pie do you prefer?!
> C: Hmm… I think I need to have another slice.
> C: I'm really hungry. I stayed up all night watching TV, and I forgot to eat!
> Lin continues eating.
> B: So… who is the winner?!
> A: I let you live in my apartment for free, remember?
> B: But I always give you free cookies!
> C: It's really hard to decide…
> Suddenly, Oscar runs to the judge's table.
> D: Sorry I'm late! I'm ready to judge the pies.
> B: Oscar, you're the judge?!
> D: Of course I'm the judge! I have the best opinions!
> A: Lin, I thought you were the judge!
> C: I never said that.
> B: But you were standing at the judge's table!
> C: I was just here to charge my phone! Then you asked me to taste your pies!
> D: So where are Lucy and Vikram's pies?
> C: Sorry, I finished both of them.

## 155. I Need to Practice

> It's late at night. Eddy wakes up because Junior is loudly playing the drums.
> Eddy walks into Junior's room.
> A: Junior, it's ten p.m.! Do you have to play the drums now?
> B: But you said that I won't be a good drummer if I don't practice.
> A: I know, but you can't play the drums at night. We both need to sleep!
> B: Sorry, Dad.
> Early the next morning, the sound of drums wakes Eddy up again.
> A: Junior, why are you playing now?
> B: You said not to practice at night, but now it's morning!
> A: It's five a.m.!
> B: I'm sorry, Dad. But I really need to practice.
> A: I know you do, son, but not while I'm sleeping.
> The next day, Eddy is working in the living room. Junior starts playing the drums again.
> A: Junior!
> B: What's wrong?
> A: Do you have to play drums all the time?
> B: But you're not sleeping now.
> A: No, but I'm working, and I can't concentrate when you're playing.
> B: But I have to practice for my concert!
> A: OK, fine…
> A few days later, Eddy is at Junior's concert, and he's falling asleep.
> Another dad taps Eddy on the shoulder.
> C: Hey! Are you OK?
> A: Yeah, I'm just tired. I haven't been sleeping well.
> C: Well, you have to watch this kid play the drums! He's amazing.
> On the stage, Junior is playing a drum solo.
> A: Hey! That's my son!
> C: Really? He's great.
> A: Uh, yeah, I know! I make him practice all the time!

## 156. Going Away Party

> Oscar is moving to a new city for a new job.
> His friends are having a goodbye party for him.
> A: Thank you, everyone! I'm so lucky to have friends.
> A: I will miss you all.
> B: What will you miss about us, Oscar?
> A: Um… I'll miss hearing your alarm every morning, Lucy. It always wakes me up so early.
> B: Thanks, Oscar! I'll miss living next to you.
> A: And Eddy… I suppose I'll miss spending time with you and Junior.
> C: Actually, you promised to babysit Junior, but you never did.
> A: Oh, well. Now it's too late.
> D: What will you miss about me, Oscar?
> A: I'll miss trying new things with you, Bea.
> D: You also said you wanted to go camping with me, Oscar, but you never did.
> A: Yeah, I'm sorry we never slept outside in the cold, near spiders and bears.
> Oscar receives an email on his phone. He reads it and looks upset.
> B: Is everything OK, Oscar?
> A: No, I don't have a new job anymore, so I can't move away. And I'll have to stay at my old job.
> B: Oh no!
> A: I'm so embarrassed. What do I tell everyone?
> Lucy turns to everyone else at the party.
> B: Everyone, I have great news! Oscar is staying. He decided he will miss us too much!
> Everyone cheers.
> C: Now you can babysit Junior this weekend, Oscar!
> D: And, we can go camping next weekend! We just have to wake up early.
> B: Don't worry, Oscar. My alarm will wake you up!
> A: Great. I'm so lucky to have friends.

## 157. It's Too Expensive

> Vikram and Priti wait for a realtor outside a house with a "for sale" sign.
> A: Wow, I love this house! It's beautiful and so big!
> B: I'm not sure. It's too expensive.
> The realtor greets them.
> C: Welcome! Which room do you want to see first?
> A: Vikram loves to bake. Let's see the kitchen!
> They look around the kitchen. Priti opens the oven.
> A: Vikram, you could bake so many great cakes here!
> B: I can bake great cakes anywhere.
> C: The kitchen also has two dishwashers.
> A: Two dishwashers? How wonderful, Vikram!
> B: I prefer to wash my dishes by hand.
> The realtor takes them upstairs.
> C: There are four bedrooms!
> B: It's just the two of us. We don't need that many rooms.
> A: But look, the windows are so big!
> B: If we have big windows, then we'll have to buy a lot of cleaning products.
> B: This house is too expensive.
> C: Maybe I can talk to the owners about the price. Excuse me.
> The realtor leaves to make a call.
> A: Can you please stop complaining?
> B: You don't understand. It's part of my plan. I want the owner to lower the price.
> The realtor returns.
> C: Good news! I spoke to the owners and they'll lower the price.
> B: Amazing! Then we will buy this house!
> A: No, we won't!
> B: But I thought you loved this house?
> A: That was before you started complaining.
> A: Now I think you're right. This house has too many rooms, too many windows, and too many dishwashers!
> B: But I love the two dishwashers!
> A: I thought you preferred doing dishes by hand.
> B: No one prefers that.

## 158. The Frog

> Junior sees his classmate, Betsy, hiding a frog in their teacher's desk.
> A: Betsy, what are you doing?
> B: I'm going to scare our teacher.
> B: He'll love it! It will be a funny prank.
> A: I love pranks! I didn't realize you love them too.
> B: Don't tell him, OK?
> A: Don't worry. I won't.
> Later, their teacher sits down at his desk.
> When he opens his drawer, the frog jumps out.
> C: Ahhhhh!
> All of the kids in the class laugh.
> The frog jumps onto Betsy's desk, and Junior catches it.
> C: This is not funny! Everyone sit down!
> No one sits down.
> C: Who did this? Who put this frog inside my desk?! 
> The class becomes very quiet.
> C: Class, if no one tells me, then I will have to punish the whole class.
> Junior raises his hand and looks at Betsy.
> A: I'll tell you who did it.
> Everyone looks at Junior. Betsy looks worried.
> B: Junior! Please, don't—
> A: I put the frog inside your desk.
> Junior smiles at Betsy.
> A: I love frogs. Don't you?
> Junior picks up the frog and kisses it.
> C: Junior, you're in a lot of trouble! I'm going to call your dad right now.
> A: I don't mind.
> The teacher leaves the classroom.
> B: Thanks, Junior. That was very brave. You know, you're pretty cool!
> A: No problem! So… do you maybe want to be my girlfriend?
> B: Ew! No. You kissed a frog.

## 159. Lily's Painting

> Lily has a painting in an art show.
> A: This is so exciting! I'm so proud of you!
> B: A lot of other artists have paintings here, too. No one is going to buy mine.
> A: Of course they will! Your painting is the best one here!
> B: I don't think so.
> People enter the art gallery and start looking at the paintings.
> A: Isn't this painting amazing?
> Zari points at Lily's painting.
> B: Zari, shh!
> A: What? I just want to make sure everyone sees your painting. It's so good!
> B: Please stop. This is embarrassing.
> A: Fine. I'll stop.
> A couple stops to look at Lily's painting.
> They whisper to each other, and then they walk past the painting.
> They look at a painting of a flower next to Lily's. Then they buy it.
> A: I can't believe they just bought that flower painting.
> A: Your painting is so much better.
> An hour later, most of the paintings have been sold. Lily's painting is still on the wall.
> A: Hmm. No one bought your painting yet!
> B: Yeah, I know.
> A: Uh… I'm going to go to the bathroom.
> Zari walks over to the owner of the art gallery.
> A: Hi! I want to buy Lily's painting.
> C: Which painting is hers?
> A: That one over there. No one wants to buy it, and I really want to make Lily feel better!
> C: Oh, a lot of people want to buy that one! But I won't let them.
> A: What? Why?
> C: It's the best painting here. I'm going to buy it for myself!

## 160. I Can Do Anything

> Eddy and Bea are playing tennis.
> A: Thanks for meeting me, Bea. I'm feeling very sad lately.
> A: All of my friends from college are so successful, but I'm not.
> Eddy hits the ball.
> A: It's time for a change in my life.
> B: Please don't buy an expensive car or start wearing tight jeans.
> A: Are you joking? I don't have enough money for a fancy car.
> Eddy and Bea sit down on a bench.
> B: Eddy, are you crying? Or is that sweat on your face?
> A: Both!
> A: I never did anything important, and now it's too late.
> B: Eddy, it's not too late!
> B: You can do something important now!
> A: You don't think I'm too old?
> B: No, you just need to work hard.
> A: I can work hard!
> B: Great. Then just say, "I can do anything!"
> A: I can do anything!
> B: That's right, Eddy!
> A: And I'm going to be an Olympic tennis player!
> B: What!?
> A: The Olympics are next summer. I need to practice more.
> A: Can you meet me here every day?
> B: Uh, well… It's really hard to become an Olympic athlete, Eddy…
> A: So you don't think I'm good enough?
> B: I think you're great. But Olympic athletes start training at a very young age… Like your son Junior's age.
> A: You're right!
> B: Huh?
> A: It's not too late for Junior! I'll make him practice every day, and then he'll be an Olympic tennis player!
> B: Um, Eddy, are we talking about the same Junior who only goes outside to buy video games?!

## 161. The Long Flight

> Lin gets on a plane for a flight to Hawaii. She sits down next to another woman.
> A: Lin, is that you?! I haven't seen you since…
> B: Since you broke up with me in college.
> A: Right. Uh… I'll ask to sit in another row.
> B: No, it's cool, Jamie, you can sit here.
> A: I'm surprised to see you! You always hated to travel.
> B: That's because I used to be afraid of flying.
> B: I'm not afraid anymore.
> A: Wow, so why are you going to Hawaii?
> B: I did some research and found the best place for whale watching.
> A: You did travel research?!
> B: Yes. I actually like to research things now.
> A: That's cool. But you get sick on boats.
> B: I used to. But now I take medicine before I go sailing.
> A: I can't believe you like to sail now.
> B: After we broke up, I started doing a lot of new things.
> A: Aw, I always wanted you to try new things…
> B: And now I am!
> A: I'm glad we sat next to each other on this plane. We should hang out again.
> B: I would love that…
> A: Maybe we can go sailing together…
> B: Yes, definitely!
> B: Wow, it's like the universe brought us back together.
> A: I know!
> Just then, another woman sits down next to Jamie.
> C: Hi, honey!
> The woman kisses Jamie.
> A: Oh! Lin, this is my girlfriend, Maria.
> B: Your… girlfriend?
> A: Maria, we're going to go sailing with Lin!
> B: Thanks, universe.

## 162. The Baby Photo

> Zari runs into her neighbor Bea's apartment.
> A: Bea! Help!
> B: Zari, what's wrong? Are you OK?
> A: No! It's an emergency!
> B: Are you hurt? Are you bleeding?
> A: No, it's worse than bleeding!
> B: Worse?
> A: I accidentally sent an embarrassing picture to the cutest boy at my school.
> B: Oh no… that is worse.
> A: Right?!
> B: Show me the picture.
> A: Here it is…
> B: Is that…
> A: My baby photo? Yes, it is.
> B: Well… that's not terrible…
> A: I sent it with the text message "I have loved you since the day I was born."
> B: What?
> A: I was trying to send it to my mom.
> A: What should I do?! Tell me what to do, Bea.
> B: You can study a lot. Then, you can graduate from school early.
> B: After that, you won't have to see him again!
> A: Bea…
> B: Or you can move to another city. I can help you find a job. Do you know how to fish?
> A: Bea!
> B: Don't worry, Zari. It's embarrassing, but you were so cute!
> B: If you tell him it was an accident, he will understand.
> Zari gets a text message.
> A: It's him!
> B: What does the message say?
> A: He… doesn't recognize my number.
> B: That's great! He doesn't know the photo is from you!
> A: No, it's terrible! He doesn't even know who I am!

## 163. Moving

> Lucy is helping her granddaughter, Lin, pack her suitcases.
> A: You're finally moving out of my apartment!
> B: I feel like I just moved here.
> A: And five years later, you're finally moving out.
> A: Are you ready?
> B: I'm going to miss this comfortable couch!
> A: Now you can sleep in a real bed!
> B: And I will have a lot more roommates.
> A: You'll make some new friends!
> B: Who will wake you up when you don't hear your alarm clock?
> A: Oh… maybe I need a louder alarm clock.
> B: And who will help you carry groceries?
> A: I'm still very strong, thank you very much.
> B: And who will read the newspaper with you on Sunday mornings?
> A: Oh… I don't know.
> A: And who will eat chocolate cake with me!? And watch scary movies? And go dancing on Fridays!?
> B: I don't know!
> B: Maybe I need to stay here… for you.
> Lin looks at her suitcases. Lucy smiles.
> A: Yes… you should stay.
> B: Great!
> Lin starts unpacking her suitcases.
> A: But you can't sleep on the couch tonight. I have a date coming over!

## 164. A Fancy Wedding

> Lucy and her granddaughter Lin are at a fancy wedding.
> A: There are too many flowers here. At your mother's wedding, there was one simple rose on every table.
> B: Shhh! Grandma, be quiet! The bride will hear you.
> A: Achoo! Good! She should know there are too many flowers. I can't stop sneezing!
> B: I think the flowers are nice.
> A: But they don't match these silver plates.
> B: I think the silver plates are fancy.
> A: At your mother's wedding, there were gold plates.
> B: Oh, I didn't know that… Tell me more about Mom's wedding.
> A: I've never told you anything about it?
> A: Well, all the men wore blue suits.
> B: That sounds very stylish!
> A: And there was a violin player.
> B: Wow. That's romantic.
> A: And during the ceremony, your mother sang a song for your father.
> B: Really? My mom did that?
> A: Yes!
> B: Grandma… are you crying?
> B: Wow, my parents' wedding sounds like it was really beautiful.
> A: No, that's not why I'm crying.
> A: I'm crying because I just saw that there's no cake.

## 165. I'm Driving

> Bea is waiting for Lin in front of her apartment building.
> Lin arrives at the apartment on a motorcycle.
> A: Are you ready to go to the beach?
> B: What is that?
> A: It's my motorcycle!
> B: I thought that you were going to rent a car.
> A: Renting a car is very expensive, but riding my motorcycle is free.
> A: Now get on.
> B: You want me to ride on the back of your motorcycle?
> A: What's wrong? Are you scared?
> B: I'm not scared of anything.
> B: Except for hairless cats.
> A: If you're not scared, then let's go.
> B: OK, but I'm driving.
> A: You want to drive my motorcycle?
> B: Of course.
> A: Bea! Why do you always have to control everything?
> A: Why can't you relax?
> B: I will relax… when you let me drive.
> B: Lin, do you want to go to the beach or not?
> A: Yes, I do.
> Later, Bea is driving the motorcycle, and Lin is riding behind her.
> Lin looks very unhappy.
> B: You were right. This is better than renting a car!
> A: And you were right, riding back here is not fun.

## 166. The Reunion

> Lucy is getting ready for a date. Her granddaughter, Lin, walks in the room.
> A: Lin! Should I wear the black dress or the green dress?
> B: The black dress is a little… short.
> A: Perfect! I'll wear the black dress!
> B: Well, you do have great legs.
> B: Where are you going?
> A: I have a date tonight!
> B: Did you meet him on the Internet?
> A: Actually, I have known him for fifty years.
> B: Fifty years?!
> A: Yes! We went to high school together. I remember he had the most beautiful brown hair.
> A: I haven't seen him since then….
> B: Wait… are you nervous? I can't believe it!
> A: I'm not nervous! Do I look nervous?
> B: A little, yes. Why are you nervous?!
> A: Well… so much has changed in fifty years!
> B: I know! The Internet, cell phones, frozen yogurt—
> A: No, no… we are not young anymore.
> B: Grandma, you are still very beautiful!
> A: I'm not talking about me! I'm worried about him!
> A: Maybe he lost all of his beautiful hair!

## 167. Move the Bed

> Zari is lying on Lily's bed. She's looking up at the ceiling.
> A: Lily, your room is boring. You should move your furniture.
> B: No. The room looks good now.
> A: I think your bed would look great in that corner.
> B: I do not.
> A: You know, it's really dangerous to have your bed next to the window.
> B: Dangerous?
> A: Lightning could hit that tree outside, and it could fall through your window.
> A: Or a murderer could climb into your room!
> B: Wow, Zari. You've thought a lot about this.
> A: I'm trying to be a good friend, Lily. I want you to be safe.
> B: I'm fine. My bed has always been next to the window.
> A: Always? Then don't you want to try something new?
> B: You know I hate new things.
> A: Well… I read a book once that said it's good to sleep with your head on the north side of your room.
> B: This is the north side of my room.
> A: Oh, did I say north side? I mean south side.
> B: Ugh, Zari! Why do you want me to move my bed?
> A: I think it will look so nice!
> B: Fine. Help me move it.
> They start to move Lily's bed, but Lily sees something on the carpet…
> B: Zari, did you spill coffee on my carpet?
> A: Yes. But don't worry. You won't see it after we move your bed.

## 168. The New App

> Lucy is exercising. Lin walks in the room with her cell phone.
> A: Grandma! Look, I have a new app on my phone!
> B: You always have a new app on your phone.
> A: But this app tells you if you're healthy!
> B: I already know I'm healthy.
> A: Question one: How many steps did you take today?
> B: Ten thousand.
> A: Wow, really? I only took… twenty-seven steps today.
> A: Question two: Do you eat healthy food?
> B: Yes, and I only eat dessert on special occasions.
> A: I always eat dessert….
> A: Question three: How many glasses of water do you drink every day?
> B: Nine!
> B: I love water! I'm like a fish.
> A: Nine? I only drink two glasses of water every day…
> A: Question four: How many hours do you sleep every night?
> B: I usually sleep for ten hours. But if I go dancing, I only sleep for eight hours.
> A: Eight hours?!
> A: Question five: Do you feel stressed?
> B: Only when my granddaughter asks too many questions!
> A: But Grandma, you're getting older!
> B: Maybe you should take the test.
> A: Me? Why?
> B: Because you don't sleep enough, you don't eat healthy food, and you don't drink enough water!

## 169. That's Not Dinner

> Vikram runs into his neighbor's apartment.
> A: Eddy, I'm here! What's the emergency?!
> B: I have a date, but I forgot she is a vegetarian… like you!
> A: That is not an emergency!
> B: But I really like her!
> A: OK, I'll help you.
> A: A vegetarian dinner is easy to make!
> Vikram opens the refrigerator.
> A: Hmm… your refrigerator is full of meat.
> A: Chicken, beef, pork… Why do you have so much meat?!
> B: Because I exercise a lot! I need to eat meat for my muscles!
> A: Do you have anything else?
> B: Yogurt!
> A: Eddy, yogurt is not dinner.
> B: I also have… cereal?
> A: Eddy, cereal is not dinner! Where are all the vegetables?
> B: Did you look in the back of the refrigerator?
> A: Oh! I see something green!
> B: Actually, I think that's Junior's science experiment.
> A: You should go to the supermarket.
> B: She'll be here in thirty minutes!
> B: I don't have time to go to the supermarket!
> Junior walks into the kitchen.
> C: Hi, Vikram. Hi, Dad.
> C: What's wrong?
> A: He's worried because his date is a vegetarian.
> C: So?
> B: We don't have any food to make a vegetarian dinner!
> C: That's not true. We have ice cream.
> A: Junior, that's not dinner.
> C: Yes, it is! Dad and I eat ice cream for dinner all the time!

## 170. Eddy's New Haircut

> Eddy sees Lucy outside their apartment building.
> A: Whoa, Eddy! What happened to your hair?
> B: Oh, I got a new haircut!
> A: Well, you need to fix it.
> A: Can you go to a hairstylist?
> B: No, I have a date right now…
> B: Oh no!
> B: This is really bad!
> A: Actually, maybe the haircut is OK…
> A: Turn your head to the right.
> Eddy turns his head. Lucy looks closely.
> A: No. Turn your head the other way.
> Eddy turns his head the other way.
> A: No, sorry, it looks bad from every angle.
> A: I hope you can get your money back from your hairstylist.
> B: It was free.
> A: Someone should tell your hairstylist to find a new career.
> B: You just told him.
> A: What?
> B: I cut my own hair.
> B: I watched a video on the Internet.
> B: It looked easy.
> A: Eddy, you have to cancel your date.
> B: It's OK. I brought my favorite hat!
> Eddy puts on his hat. Lucy looks worried.
> B: What's wrong now?
> A: Uh… well…
> A: Do you have a different hat?
> B: Why?
> A: That hat is worse than the haircut.

## 171. The Wedding Present

> Vikram is dancing in his living room.
> A: Oh, yeah! Step to the left! Step to the right! I love this song!
> He accidentally hits a vase. It falls on the floor and breaks.
> A: Oh no! Maybe I can fix it!
> He picks up the pieces of the vase.
> A: This piece goes here… this piece goes there… oh no. This looks terrible.
> His wife, Priti, walks into the room. Vikram tries to hide the vase.
> B: Vikram! Did you break that vase?
> B: Were you dancing again?
> A: Yes. But don't worry! I can fix it! Look!
> Vikram shows her pieces of the vase.
> B: Oh, honey. I don't think we can fix it.
> A: I know, I'm so sorry. I know it was your favorite.
> B: My favorite?
> A: Yes. Because it was a wedding present from your sister.
> B: She didn't give us this vase. She gave us a picture frame.
> A: Oh, right! Did your mother give us the vase?
> B: No, she gave us that clock you broke last month, when you were doing yoga.
> A: Oh, right.
> B: Maybe it's from your cousin.
> A: But the vase is so ugly!
> B: I know. That's why I thought your cousin gave it to us.
> A: Ha! Wait, you also think the vase is ugly?
> B: It's terrible.
> A: Now I'm not sorry that I broke it!
> B: Yes, the living room looks much better without it.
> B: And now we have more space for dancing!
> Vikram turns on the music, and they start dancing.
> B: Step to the left… Oh yeah!

## 172. Waiting for George

> Lucy is leaving a nice restaurant.
> She sees her friend, Julia, sitting at a table by herself.
> A: Julia! What's wrong? You look sad!
> B: Oh Lucy, it's awful! It's my anniversary, but I don't think George is coming.
> A: What? Why not?
> B: I forgot our anniversary last year, and I think he's still angry about it. He's very late.
> A: But that was a year ago!
> A: He's probably late because of traffic.
> B: No, he's not coming…
> B: And look at everything I did for him this year. I got his favorite flowers.
> B: And I hired a musician to play his favorite song.
> Julia points to a violin player at a nearby table.
> B: The musician has been waiting for an hour.
> A: George is an hour late?! Maybe he isn't coming…
> B: He was so angry when I forgot our anniversary last year.
> B: This year, I remembered everything. But he's not here! Now I know our relationship is finished.
> A: Julia, George is terrible. You can find five men in this restaurant who are better than him.
> B: You don't like George?
> A: I have never liked George! He talks too much.
> Julia gets a text message.
> B: Oh, George just texted me!
> B: He says, "I'm so excited for our anniversary tomorrow."
> B: What?! Our anniversary is the fifteenth!
> A: Julia, tomorrow is the fifteenth.
> B: Oh! My anniversary is tomorrow!
> B: I feel much better now!
> A: Oh, great! Everything is OK with you and George!
> B: Yes! I'm so happy. But wait, do you really think George talks too much?

## 173. Marathon Runner

> Eddy is on a date with Mimi at a restaurant.
> A: The dinner was very delicious.
> B: Yes, it was!
> B: Have I told you I'm going to run a marathon in the fall?
> A: Yes. You told me three times.
> B: I'm running a marathon in the fall!
> A: Now, you've told me four times.
> B: Maybe our next date should be at the park!
> A: That sounds romantic! We can look at the birds, and drink wine and—
> B: And we can run together!
> A: Or we can go to the new Italian restaurant downtown!
> B: I don't like that restaurant. I'm not allowed to wear my sneakers there.
> B: Have you seen my new sneakers? I bought these for the marathon.
> A: Yes… you already showed me your sneakers.
> B: These are perfect for running in any kind of weather!
> A: Interesting…
> B: I hope it doesn't rain on the day of the marathon.
> A: Well, it's late. I think I'm ready to go home now.
> B: This was fun! Do you want to get coffee tomorrow?
> A: Hmmm… Yes, come to the coffee shop tomorrow. I have a surprise for you.
> The next day Eddy is at the coffee shop. He's waiting for Mimi, but she doesn't arrive.
> A woman runs over to Eddy.
> C: Hi! Are you Eddy?
> B: Yes…
> C: I'm Deborah. My friend, Mimi, said we should meet!
> B: Hi, I'm Eddy. I like your sneakers!
> C: Thanks! I'm running a marathon in the fall!

## 174. Aliens Are Real

> Eddy and his son, Junior, are in their apartment.
> They are arguing.
> A: I think believing in aliens is crazy.
> B: Crazy?
> B: Thousands of people have seen aliens.
> A: Thousands of people can be wrong.
> B: The government says aliens are real.
> A: The government is wrong about a lot of things.
> B: Do you know how big the universe is?
> A: It's pretty big.
> B: Pretty big?
> B: There are billions of planets.
> A: So?
> B: There are definitely aliens on one of those planets.
> A: We'll never know.
> B: All the smartest scientists believe aliens are real.
> A: None of the scientists I know believe in aliens.
> B: How many scientists do you know?
> A: OK, I don't know any scientists…
> B: Dad, you know it's possible that aliens are real.
> A: Fine, maybe it's possible.
> A: But I still don't believe that aliens ate all of my favorite cereal.
> B: How do you know that, Dad?
> A: I believe in what I see. And I see milk on your shirt.
> B: What?
> Junior looks down at his shirt.
> B: OK, you win. I ate your cereal.
> B: But I still think aliens are real.

## 175. Space Viking

> Lily and Zari are in art class.
> A: I'm so excited to see Space Viking 2 tonight!
> Their teacher, Oscar, hears them talking about the movie.
> B: Space Viking?!
> B: Please don't tell me you are going to see that movie!
> C: Yes. Tonight.
> B: Tonight?! You're artists. You shouldn't watch action movies.
> A: We enjoy action movies.
> C: They're stupid, but they're fun.
> B: When you watch those kinds of movies, you don't learn anything.
> B: You should watch artistic and intelligent movies.
> A: That sounds boring.
> B: I have two tickets to the international film festival tonight. Please, take them!
> C: OK, we'll think about it.
> Later, Zari and Lily are outside the movie theater.
> A: Wow, look at all the people here to see Space Viking 2!
> C: Is that… our teacher?
> Oscar is outside the movie theater, wearing a Space Viking costume.
> The girls walk over to him.
> A: Sir! Are you here to see Space Viking 2?
> B: Uh… No?
> C: Then why are you wearing that costume?
> A: You're a Space Viking fan!
> B: Maybe I am.
> C: You said we wouldn't learn anything.
> A: But we learned that our art teacher likes action movies!
> B: I just wanted to watch my movie alone.
> C: OK. See you on Monday, Space Viking…

## 176. Bad Reception

> Eddy and Oscar are in Oscar's apartment. They are watching a soccer game on TV.
> A: Yes! Amazing!
> A: Did you see that goal?
> B: No. Eddy, you asked to come into my apartment for one minute to check the score.
> B: But you've been here an hour!
> A: I know. Aren't you glad I stayed?
> B: Eddy, I am very tired.
> A: Some pizza will wake you up.
> B: No, it's too late for pizza!
> A: Don't worry! I know an amazing pizza place that's open late.
> Eddy takes out his phone.
> A: Hmm… I don't have any reception. Does your phone have reception?
> Oscar looks at his phone. It has great reception.
> B: No, sorry.
> B: But there's good reception near my front door.
> Eddy walks over to the door.
> A: There's still no reception here.
> B: Can you try walking out the door?
> A: You want me to go into the hall?
> B: Yes! The reception is great there.
> Eddy opens the door and walks out of the apartment.
> A: There is great reception in the hall!
> Oscar runs to the door, shuts it quickly, and locks it.
> B: He's finally gone!
> Oscar's phone rings.
> Oscar answers his phone. It's Eddy calling from the hall.
> A: Oscar? Your door is locked. Can you let me in?
> B: Sorry, I can't hear you. I have bad reception.

## 177. A Perfect Anniversary

> Vikram walks into a jewelry store.
> A: Hello, how can I help you?
> B: Hi! I need help with something very special.
> B: I just drove all the way to this city. Twenty years ago, I met my wife here!
> A: Wow! Twenty years is such a long time!
> B: Yes, it is! I'm planning the perfect anniversary.
> A: Great, I can help you with that!
> B: Thanks! So, I'm looking for—
> A: Don't tell me! I already know.
> B: You do?
> A: Yes! You need a silver necklace! You can take your wife on a boat at sunset and give it to her. That will be very romantic.
> B: Actually, no—
> A: You're right. The anniversary has to be perfect.
> A:  A gold necklace is much better!
> B: No, no—
> A: Earrings? Look at these beautiful diamond earrings here.
> B: Diamond earrings? No. We don't usually spend more than five dollars on anniversary presents.
> A: What?
> B: We love each other and we don't care about fancy presents.
> A: Then why are you in a jewelry store?
> Vikram takes a napkin out of his pocket. It has the name of a sandwich shop on it.
> B: Do you know where this sandwich shop is? I can't find the address online. I need to buy my wife a sandwich there for our anniversary.
> A: A sandwich? That's not very romantic.
> B: Well, we shared a sandwich there on our first date.
> A: You kept this napkin for twenty years?!
> B: Yes! I have loved her since we shared that sandwich.
> A: OK… maybe that is romantic.

## 178. The Password

> Lucy is looking at her computer.
> A: Lin! I can't log into my computer! I forgot my password.
> B: OK, I'll look at it… The password hint is "The name of your first love."
> A: Hm…
> A: Well, when I was a spy…
> A: I had to bring some medicine over the border…
> B: What?
> A: At the time, I was working with a man named Eduardo…
> B: "Eduardo?" …
> Lin types the name into the computer.
> B: That's not the password.
> A: No, I never loved Eduardo. He was stupid.
> A: Because of Eduardo, the enemies caught us.
> A: They took us to a secret room in the embassy.
> B: Uh-oh.
> A: The enemy leader came to see me. We spent days talking. Finally, he let us leave.
> B: Oh, really?
> A: We became good friends.
> B: What was his name?
> A: Jean-Luc.
> Lin types the name into the computer.
> B: That's not the password.
> A: He gave me money to get on a plane.
> B: Then what happened?
> A: Well… The pilot was a very handsome young man.
> A: Kind, funny, smart… his name was Rafael.
> B: I'll try "Rafael"… no. That's not the password.
> A: No, Rafael died.
> B: What?
> A: He had a heart attack while we were flying.
> B: Oh no!
> A: His last words were, "Take care of the Black Rose."
> A: And I did.
> B: What's the Black Rose?
> A: The airplane. It was the most beautiful plane in the world.
> B: "Black Rose…" Yes! That's the password!

## 179. Junior Makes a Mess

> Eddy comes home from work.
> A: Junior! I'm home!
> B: I'm in my room, Dad!
> Eddy goes to Junior's room. There is paint everywhere.
> A: Junior! What are you doing? You made a mess!
> B: I know! I'm working on something special.
> A: Ugh, Junior. We need to clean this room.
> B: OK, Dad…
> A: But let's make dinner first.
> Eddy and Junior walk to the kitchen. There's paint and chocolate everywhere.
> A: Junior! What did you do?!
> A: Why is there paint in here too? And what is this on the walls? Chocolate? How did you get chocolate on the walls?
> B: I was baking! It was messy.
> A: Junior, please help me clean now.
> B: But, Dad…
> A: I had a difficult day. No one at work remembered my birthday.
> A: I just wanted to come home and have a nice dinner with my son. But now we have to clean your room and the kitchen!
> B: Dad…
> A: I have a headache. I'm going to lie down on the couch.
> Eddy goes to the living room. Junior runs behind him.
> B: Wait, Dad!
> A: Junior! There's paint and chocolate in here too! You're in trouble now!
> A: Wait… is that a birthday cake?
> B: Yes!
> A: And is that a painting of … a clown?
> B: No, that's a painting of you. Happy birthday, Dad!
> A: Oh. Thank you for remembering, Junior. I love it.
> Eddy hugs Junior.
> B: Do you want to eat some cake now?
> A: Uh… maybe later, Junior. This cake is covered in paint…

## 180. The Audition

> Lily is in the hall at school. Zari runs over to her.
> A: Lily! I'm going to an audition for a play after school. Can you please come with me?
> B: No.
> A: Please? I'm too nervous to do it by myself.
> B: You'll be fine.
> A: No, I won't. If I get too nervous, I might faint.
> B: That only happens on TV.
> A: No. It happens at theater auditions.
> A: Please come with me, Lily. I need you.
> B: Ugh… OK.
> A: Thank you!
> They go to the audition at the local theater. Their art teacher, Oscar, is sitting at a table.
> B: Oh, Mr. Oscar is directing the play?
> A: That's why I was so nervous.
> C: OK, actors, are you ready to begin your audition?
> B: Wait, I have to perform with you?
> A: Of course! That's why I needed you to come. Don't worry, we can do this!
> Lily suddenly looks very worried.
> A: Lily? Are you OK?
> B: I don't feel well. I… I think I'm going to…
> Lily faints.
> A: Lily!
> Later, Lily wakes up.
> A: I told you people faint at auditions.
> B: Ugh, Zari…
> A: Thanks for going to the audition with me. And I have good news…
> A: I'm going to be in the play! After you fainted, I wasn't nervous anymore! My audition was great!
> A: And you're going to be in the play too!
> B: What? But I fainted.
> A: I know! Because you were so good at lying on the floor, they chose you to be a dead body in the play!
> B: Oh…
> B: That's actually pretty cool.

## 181. Aunt Betty

> Eddy knocks on the bathroom door.
> A: Junior, come out now. We're going to Aunt Betty's house tonight.
> B: I can't go. I'm sick.
> A: You're not sick. You just don't like Aunt Betty.
> B: You're right, I don't like her. She's mean and all of her candy is old.
> B: But I really am sick.
> A: No, you aren't.
> B: Yes, I am. My stomach hurts. My face hurts. Everything hurts!
> B: I think I'm dying.
> A: Aunt Betty will be sad if you don't come with me to visit her.
> B: I know, but she will be sadder if I die.
> A: Junior…
> B: You can go without me.
> B: I'll stay here and watch TV until I feel better.
> A: If you come with me to Aunt Betty's house, we can get ice cream.
> B: Ice cream?
> A: I'll buy you the biggest bowl of ice cream at the shop.
> B: Well… OK.
> Junior opens the door… and he looks terrible.
> A: Whoa! Wow! Junior, your face is covered in red spots!
> A: We need to go to the hospital right now!
> B: The hospital?! You told me we were going to get ice cream!

## 182. Twenty Years

> Bea is making a documentary film.
> She's interviewing Oscar, the local art teacher.
> A: Are you ready for the interview now?
> B: Yes! One more minute.
> A: You know, I canceled all of my appointments today for this.
> B: Thank you! I'm sorry you've been waiting for a while.
> A: It's OK. I've been waiting for twenty years to be in a film about art.
> B: Twenty years?!
> A: Yes. I've been an artist since I was very young. But no one has ever interviewed me.
> Bea turns on the camera.
> B: Three, two…
> B: Wait. I just need to move these lights. One moment…
> A: Did you see my new paintings in the coffee shop?
> B: No, I haven't seen them yet!
> A: Those paintings are my best work. We can talk about them in the interview.
> B: I'm sure they are great!
> B: OK, I'm ready now!
> A: Finally!
> Bea turns on the camera.
> B: Three, two…
> B: Wait! I forgot the microphone.
> A: Oh yes, I have many things to say.
> Bea puts a microphone next to Oscar.
> B: OK! I'm ready!
> Bea turns on the camera.
> B: Three, two, one!
> A: So, what would you like to know about my art?
> B: Oh! This interview isn't about your art. It's about an artist you studied with!
> A: What? I waited all day to talk about another artist?! I need to leave.
> B: But you've been waiting twenty years to talk about art!
> Oscar stands up and gets ready to leave.
> A: Yes, and I can wait a little longer.

## 183. Junior's Interview

> Junior enters Bea's apartment. He is carrying a briefcase.
> A: Hello, Bea. I'm here for my interview.
> B: Um… interview?
> A: Yes. My dad said you're going on a trip. So, I would like to apply for a job watering your plants.
> B: Ah! Please, sit down.
> A: Thank you, I will sit down.
> He sits down and opens his briefcase.
> B: Would you like a cookie?
> A: No, thank you. I don't eat during business meetings.
> B: Good, because they're my roommate's cookies. She's not happy when I eat them.
> Junior gives his résumé to Bea.
> B: Did you write this with a crayon?
> A: Yes. Yes, I did.
> B: OK. Why should I give you this job?
> A: I am very responsible. I like to work hard.
> B: Have you watered plants before?
> A: No, but I've been watching videos online.
> B: What are your goals for the future?
> A: Driving a flying car!
> A: But first I'll have my own business. And you're my first customer.
> B: Watering plants is a very big job.
> A: You only have two plants. And they're dying.
> B: Right. My roommate and I always forget to water them.
> A: Bea. Listen.
> B: Yeah?
> A: If you give me the job, you can eat all of your roommate's cookies. And then, you can tell her I ate them.
> B: Ooh. Good idea! You can have the job!
> They shake hands.
> A: We can talk about my salary later.

## 186. Nice Tie

> A: Yes, I think that's all for you.

## 187. The Accident

> Junior sees Lucy in their neighborhood.
> A: Hi Lucy!
> Lucy waves at Junior. She has a bandage on her foot.
> A: Why do you have a bandage on your foot?
> B: I had an accident yesterday.
> A: An accident? What happened?
> B: Well, I woke up in the morning and made tea.
> B: And I dropped the pot of hot water.
> A: Did you burn your foot?
> B: No, but the water spilled on the floor and the pot broke.
> A: Oh.
> B: After that, I had to buy a new pot, so I got on my motorcycle. While I was riding, a cow walked into the road!
> A: Oh no! Did you hit the cow? Is that how you hurt your foot?
> B: No, but I had to stop very quickly. I fell off my motorcycle!
> A: Oh, so that's how you hurt your foot!
> B: No. After I fell, my motorcycle wasn't working, so I walked to find help.
> B: And then a huge dog started running towards me.
> A: Did the dog bite you?
> B: No, he was very friendly!
> A: OK…
> B: Then a nice man saw me on the road and stopped to help me.
> B: He was very handsome, so I asked him to go out with me.
> A: But how did you hurt your foot?!
> B: He stepped on it! I'll never go dancing with him again.

## 188. Late for the Movie

> Lucy is buying popcorn at the movie theater. She sees a man and a woman. She waves at them.
> A: John? John! Hello!
> The man grabs the woman's hand and starts to walk away quickly.
> A: John, wait! It's me, Lucy!
> Lucy runs over to them.
> B: Oh, hi, Lucy… It's good to see you but sorry, we need to go sit down.
> A: Movies never start on time.
> A:  Stay for a minute.
> C: Sure!
> B: Uh… sure.
> A: It's been a long time! How have you been?
> B: Uh… fine. And you?
> A: I'm good! I just started boxing, and I love it!
> Lucy turns to the woman and smiles.
> A: And you look great! Did you change your hair color? You look so good with blonde hair!
> C: No, this is the color my hair has always been.
> A: Really? And you stopped wearing glasses! It makes you look so much younger.
> C: I've never worn glasses…
> B: We really need to leave for that movie…
> A: Actually, you look a lot younger now! What is your secret?
> C: I'm sorry, but we've never met before.
> A: What? Of course we've met. I was a guest at your wedding.
> C: What wedding? John and I aren't married.
> A: That's funny, Sandra.
> C: My name is Shirley! Who's Sandra?!
> B: Oh hey! The movie is starting now! We have to go!
> C: John? Who is Sandra?!
> Lucy starts eating her popcorn.
> A: Oh, wow. John, my friend, I think you're going to miss that movie.

## 189. Is This a Date？

> Junior and Lily are at a museum.
> A: This museum is pretty cool…
> B: It's a really great museum! And this is a great date!
> A: What? Junior, this is not a date.
> B: But it's just the two of us. Alone!
> A: That doesn't mean it's a date.
> A: We went to the library together on Wednesday, and that wasn't a date.
> B: Wait… that wasn't a date either?
> A: No, Junior! I'm your babysitter, not your date.
> B: Well, I'm confused. What usually happens during a date?
> A: Well, uh… A date happens at a place like… a restaurant.
> B: But we went to a sandwich shop for lunch!
> A: No, not a sandwich shop. A fancy restaurant.
> B: But you bought my sandwich…
> A: Your dad gave me the money for your sandwich.
> A: It's also the afternoon right now. Dates don't happen during the day.
> A week later, Junior sees Lily at the movie theater.
> B: Hi Lily! You're seeing this movie too?
> A: Oh, hi, Junior.
> B: Wow, that's a lot of popcorn for one person!
> A: OK, you can sit next to me and eat some of my popcorn.
> A: But no talking. And remember—
> B: I know, I know. It's not a date!
> B: Anyway, I already have a date tonight.
> Zari walks over to Junior and Lily. She has two sodas and a box of candy.
> C: Look, Junior! Your dad gave me enough money to buy candy too!
> B: Thank you, Zari. This is a great date!
> C: Junior, this is not a date.

## 190. The Art Show

> Oscar waits in a long line for an art show downtown.
> He walks over to the security guard.
> A: I've been waiting in line since seven o'clock! Can I go in now?
> B: Sir, this is a very famous artist. You need to wait.
> Oscar continues to wait. Then, the security guard waves at a man in a leather jacket. He lets the man inside the building.
> A: Hey! I was here before that man!
> B: Yeah. But he's cool. Look at what he's wearing.
> Oscar gets an idea. He runs into a store nearby and buys a new jacket. He walks over to the security guard again.
> A: Now will you let me in?
> The security guard looks at Oscar wearing his new jacket.
> B: That's a great jacket. But no, you still can't go in.
> The security guard lets a man and a woman go into the building.
> A: Those people just got here!
> B: It's cold. I didn't want them to wait outside for a long time.
> A: I'm cold! I've been waiting outside for hours!
> B: But now you have a warm jacket.
> A: Ugh!
> A: Will you let me inside if I give you… this?
> Oscar tries to give the security guard five dollars.
> B: Five dollars? Are you joking?
> B: Please go back to the end of the line.
> A: Ugh, fine.
> Oscar sees his friend Lucy and waves at her.
> A: Hey, Lucy! You're here for the art show too?! I've been waiting in line for hours.
> C: You have?
> A: Yeah, but I'm giving up now. Let's go get dinner instead.
> C: Sure. I'm really hungry after looking at all of that art.
> A: What? You got inside?
> B: Of course. She's very cool.

## 191. Whale Watching

> Eddy and his son, Junior, are whale watching on a boat. Junior is playing a video game on his phone.
> A: Isn't this terrific, Junior? I can't wait until we see a whale!
> B: I can't wait to get to the next level of my game!
> A: Junior, why aren't you paying attention? A whale could jump out of the water at any time!
> Junior looks at the ocean, then he looks back at his game.
> B: I don't see any whales.
> A: You have to be patient and watch the water!
> B: But I'm almost on level fifty in my game now!
> A: I can't believe you don't care about this.
> A woman walks over to Eddy.
> C: My daughter isn't paying attention either.
> She points at her daughter, who is texting on her phone.
> A: I don't understand. When I was a kid, I loved whale watching.
> C: I loved whale watching too!
> A: My name's Eddy. And you are…?
> C: Well hello, Eddy. I'm Sofia.
> A: Nice to meet you, Sofia.
> C: It's great to meet another parent who understands.
> A: Yes, kids never pay attention to important things!
> Behind Eddy, a giant whale jumps out of the water. Junior screams.
> B: Oh, wow! Dad, look!
> A: Junior, I don't want to hear about your video game right now.
> Another whale jumps out of the water behind them.
> D: Mom! You missed it!
> C: What?!
> B: You missed the whales!
> A: No!
> B: Adults never pay attention to important things!

## 192. I Can Fix It!

> Oscar is standing outside his classroom. He looks upset. Another teacher, Eddy, walks by.
> A: Hi, Oscar! Is everything OK?
> B: No. I called someone to fix the bathroom sink at my house, but he's very late.
> A: You have a problem with your bathroom sink? I can fix it!
> B: No, thanks. I want to call a professional.
> A: I fix things in my house all the time! Come on, you'll save money!
> B: Hmm… I can save some money?
> After school, Oscar and Eddy go to Oscar's house.
> A: Your house is so fancy.
> A: It should be in a magazine!
> B: Thank you. It was in a magazine last year.
> A: I love your gold bathroom mirror ! And your towels are so white!
> B: Yes, and very expensive.
> A: Wow, this vase is nice, too! Putting flowers on top of the toilet is a great idea.
> B: Eddy, are you going to fix the sink?
> A: Oh! Yes, of course.
> Eddy walks towards the sink. He accidentally hits the vase. It falls on the floor and breaks.
> A: Oh no! Sorry…
> B: It's OK. Just fix the sink, please.
> Eddy starts to fix the sink. Water spills on the floor. Eddy grabs a towel.
> B: No! Eddy!
> B: Don't use my expensive towels!
> Eddy stands up quickly and hits the mirror. It falls off the wall and breaks.
> A: Oops.
> B: My new mirror!
> A: OK… I'm finished. Look! I fixed the sink!
> B: Thanks. But you broke my vase and my mirror. My towels are dirty. And there's water everywhere!
> A: But you didn't have to pay to fix your sink!

## 193. Hannah's Party

> Zari is at a party at her friend Hannah's house. Lily arrives at the party.
> A: Lily! What are you doing here? You hate parties.
> B: I heard that Hannah is moving away.
> A: I didn't know that you were friends with Hannah.
> Lily walks through the house looking for Hannah. Zari follows her.
> A: You didn't come to my party last week.
> B: I need to see Hannah before she moves away.
> Lily opens a door and sees two teenagers kissing.
> B: Ew.
> She closes the door and continues walking.
> A: Wait, is Hannah secretly your best friend?
> They walk past a pool. A tall boy gets out of the water and comes over to them.
> C: Lily! You're at a party?
> B: Go away. I'm busy.
> Lily pushes the boy into the pool.
> A: OK. Let's find your best friend Hannah now. You can tell her you'll miss her so much.
> Lily and Zari see a girl standing in the kitchen.
> B: Hey, Jamie. Have you seen Hannah?
> D: She's over there.
> B: Come on, Zari. Let's go talk to Hannah. And stop being jealous.
> A: I'm not jealous. It's OK that you like Hannah more than you like me…
> B: Zari…
> They walk over to Hannah.
> E: Lily! I'm surprised to see you. Don't you hate parties?
> A: She does hate parties, but she really wanted to see you.
> E: Really?
> A: Yes, because Lily's your best friend, right?
> E: Uh… no.
> A: Then why are you here, Lily?
> B: I'm here because Hannah owes me twenty dollars. I wanted to get it before she moved.
> A: Ohhhhh!
> A: Hannah! You need to give my best friend Lily her money now!

## 194. Eddy's Meeting

> Eddy is meeting with his son Junior's teacher. He sits down and looks nervous.
> A: Thank you for coming in. We really need to talk.
> B: What did Junior do? Has he been hiding under his desk and eating candy again?
> A: No, that's not why I called you—
> B: Oh no. Did he bring frogs to class in his backpack again?
> A: Well, yes, but that's not why I called you.
> B: Oh. Then, what is the problem?
> A: We need to talk about Junior's homework.
> B: Ah. I understand.
> B: I've been trying to help Junior with his homework more often.
> A: Well, this week—
> B: Actually, this week I helped him with his science project!
> A: Oh, you helped him with his project?
> B: Yes! I helped him because I know a lot about dinosaurs.
> A: You do?
> B: Yes. I've seen every dinosaur movie.
> A: Ah. Well, Junior's homework is usually very good…
> B: That's great!
> A: But his dinosaur project was terrible.
> A: A lot of the information was wrong.
> A: For example, humans did not ride dinosaurs.
> B: Oh… right, I knew that.
> A: Also, dinosaurs could not run faster than cars.
> B: Really?
> A: Maybe you should let Junior do the research next time.

## 195. I'm the Manager

> Lily arrives at the clothing store where she works. Her boss immediately comes to talk to her.
> A: Lily, you're late again.
> B: I know.
> A: We need to have a serious conversation.
> B: Alright.
> A: There's always a mess in the store when you're working.
> B: If I clean the store, the customers make it messy again, so I just wait until the end of the day to clean. 
> A: But you never clean the store at the end of the day.
> B: That's true. 
> A: And the music you play is too loud.
> B: I play loud music so the customers can't talk to me.
> A: That's another thing. You are so mean to the customers!
> A customer walks over to Lily.
> C: Excuse me, do you have this shirt in a different color?
> B: No, go away.
> C: Haha, you're so funny. Bye!
> A: That's exactly what I'm talking about.
> B: So… am I going to lose my job?
> A: No. Unfortunately, you're the best employee that I have. I'm giving you a promotion. 
> B: Really?
> A: I don't know why, but all our customers love you. 
> A: They think you're cool, and they love loud music. And then they spend a lot of money here.
> B: That's really funny.
> A: So, starting today, you're going to be a manager.
> A: You'll have to make the work schedule for all the employees.
> B: Ew.
> A: But you will make more money.
> B: That's cool.
> A: And you need to be the first person here every morning.
> B: I'm not going to do that.
> A: I know.
> B: Thanks for the promotion. Bye.
> A: Wait, you just got here! Where are you going?
> B: I decided I'm not working today. I'm the manager now.

## 196. Is Your Wifi Working？

> It's late at night. Eddy's neighbor, Bea, knocks on his door.
> A: Oh, hi, Bea! Why are you here so late?
> B: Hi, Eddy. I was wondering… is your wifi working?
> A: It isn't! How did you know?
> B: My wifi stopped working, too. I just wanted to make sure you were OK.
> A: Oh, you're such a good friend!
> B: Would you like me to come inside and fix it for you?
> A: You mean right now? Um… sure!
> Bea walks into Eddy's apartment and looks around.
> B: OK, did you try turning it off and on?
> A: Turning what off and on?
> B: Your router.
> A: My what?
> B: Never mind.
> Bea looks for Eddy's router.
> A: You know, my walls are very thick here. Maybe that's the problem!
> B: No, that's not the problem. Your wifi is very strong in my apartment.
> A: It is?
> B: I mean, I think it is.
> A: Wait, why are you really here?
> B: Because your wifi isn't working.
> B: And… my wifi isn't working because your wifi isn't working.
> A: Huh?
> B: Eddy, I use your wifi.
> A: What?
> B: And I was just watching a really good movie. There were only five minutes left!
> A: You use my wifi?
> B: Yes. Now, can I please try to fix your wifi so I can finish my movie?
> A: OK.
> There is another knock on Eddy's door. Eddy answers it. Lin is standing outside.
> A: Oh, hi, Lin! Why are you here so late?
> C: Hi, Eddy. Uh… I was wondering. Is your wifi working?

## 197. The Worst Season

> Oscar and Vikram are waiting for a bus.
> Oscar sneezes.
> A: Ugh. I have very bad allergies right now.
> B: Yeah, your eyes look really red!
> A: I always feel terrible during spring.
> B: Well, summer will be here soon.
> A: Why is that a good thing?
> B: Because then you won't have allergies anymore.
> A: But summer is so hot.
> A: I hate seeing everyone wear shorts.
> B: OK. Then you probably like fall!
> A: Definitely not.
> B: Why?
> A: Fall is the worst season.
> A: I'm a teacher! I have to go back to work again in fall.
> B: Well, do you like winter?
> A: Winter is the worst season.
> B: You just said fall is the worst season.
> A: Winter is freezing.
> A: And the weather makes my skin so dry!
> B: Oscar, do you like any part of the year?
> A: New Year's Eve is OK.
> B: Great! Why do you like New Year's Eve?
> A: Because on New Year's Eve another terrible year is finally over.

## 198. Call a Doctor!

> Eddy is jogging in the neighborhood. Suddenly, he falls and hurts his ankle.
> A: Ow!
> A man in a white lab coat walks quickly past him.
> A: Hey! Doctor! Doctor!
> B: Who, me?
> A: Yes, can you help me?
> B: I'm actually late, I need to go to work.
> A: But my ankle hurts a lot. Please help me!
> B: Well… OK.
> B: I'll just take off your shoe…
> B: Wow! This looks bad!
> A: Oh no. What's wrong?
> B: You really need to cut your toenails!
> B: But let me have a look at your ankle. Hm. I'm going to try to move it.
> A: What? No—Ow!
> B: OK, that was a bad idea. Did it hurt?
> A: Yes!
> B: Oops. Hmm. Maybe I can make a bandage.
> He tears a piece of Eddy's shirt.
> A: Hey! My shirt!
> B: I need it to make a bandage. I'm going to put it around your ankle.
> A: Ow! That's too tight!
> B: If you're going to complain about everything, I'm not going to help you.
> A: What? Don't doctors have to help people when they're hurt?
> B: I don't know, I'm not a doctor.
> A: You said you were a doctor.
> B: No, I didn't. I'm an actor.
> A: Why are you wearing a lab coat?
> B: I'm a doctor on a TV show, and I'm wearing my costume.
> A: Wait, I've seen you on the TV show you're on! My son and I watch it!
> A: I know how you can help me feel better…
> B: How?
> A: You can take a picture with me for my son!

## 199. Lin's Resume

> Lin is meeting a woman at a cafe for a job interview. She sits down and gives the woman her resume.
> A: Thank you for meeting me, Lin. You have a very interesting resume.
> A: It says that your first job was studying whales in Antarctica.
> B: Yes, I wrote that on my resume.
> A: What kind of whales did you study?
> B: There's more than one kind of whale? Uh… I studied… the biggest whales.
> A: OK… And then your next job was… working in a morgue in Paris?
> B: Doesn't that sound like a cool job? I've wanted to do that since I was a little girl.
> A: Really?
> A: You seem… very young. Do you need years of training to work in a morgue?
> B: I forgot. I've had a lot of interesting jobs.
> A: Next, you wrote on your resume that you were a firefighter in San Diego…
> B: Yes, I did!
> A: I have a brother who is a firefighter there. Sam Watkins. Do you know him?
> B: Of course, I know Sam! He's great!
> A: Lin, I lied. I don't have a brother.
> B: Oops.
> A: So… are any of the jobs on your resume real?
> B: No. All of my real jobs were pretty boring.
> A: Well, I'm sorry. I can't give you this job.
> B: Yeah, I understand…
> A: But I do have a suggestion.
> A: Have you ever thought about a career in creative writing?

## 200. The Great Baking Show

> Vikram and his friend, Lin, are at a TV studio. They are having an audition for a new baking show.
> A: Thanks for being my assistant today, Lin.
> B: No problem. I know how important this is to you. And I brought some extra ingredients to help us win.
> A: What? If we want to succeed, we need to follow my recipe exactly.
> B: Trust me, I watch a lot of baking shows. If you want to win, you have to do something special!
> The producer makes an announcement.
> C: You have one hour to bake your cakes. Go!
> A: Please follow my recipe, Lin! Just add the flour and sugar…
> Lin adds the flour and sugar—and some small pieces of cheese.
> A: No!
> B: Cheese will make this cake much more interesting.
> A: I don't want an interesting cake!
> B: And I added beet juice. It's bright red!
> A: Lin!
> C: Bakers! It's time to put your cakes in the oven.
> A: Maybe it will be OK…
> While the cake bakes, Lin puts a scarf around Vikram's neck.
> B: If you want to be on TV, then you need to look cool.
> A: We need to pay attention to the cake. I don't want it to burn… Oh no!
> Vikram takes the cake out of the oven. It's on fire.
> B: Use the scarf!
> Vikram uses the scarf to stop the fire. The scarf catches on fire as the producers laugh.
> A: Oh no, they're laughing at us. We should just go.
> Vikram gets ready to leave, but the producer stops him.
> C: Don't go! We want you to be on our show!
> B: Really?
> A: But we burned our cake…
> C: Yes, but you and Lin are so fun to watch!

## 201. The Refund

> Lily is working at the clothing store.
> A: Excuse me, how much is this suit?
> B: Two hundred dollars. Do you want to try the suit on?
> A: No, I don't have time. Just take my money!
> The man buys the suit. The next day, he returns to the store.
> A: Excuse me! I want a refund for this suit.
> B: Why? Is there a problem?
> A: This is not a black suit!
> B: You're right. That's a blue suit.
> A: I came here to buy a black suit.
> B: OK, so why did you buy a blue suit?
> A: Look at my family photo!
> The man shows Lily his family photo.
> A: My wife is wearing a black dress in this photo. She told me to wear a black suit to match her dress!
> B: I'm sorry, dude. You can't return the suit if you wore it.
> A: I only wore the suit for an hour!
> B: Read the bottom of the receipt.
> He reads the receipt.
> A: "No refunds if you wear the clothing."
> A: But the suit didn't even fit me! It was so uncomfortable!
> B: Listen, I'm sorry. I can't give you a refund unless there was a problem. Like, if the suit was damaged—
> A: I can get a refund if the suit is damaged? Well, fine! Look!
> He tears the sleeve off of the suit.
> B: Dude! That's not cool.
> A: I want my two hundred dollars back!
> The store manager runs over to the cash register.
> C: What is the problem?
> C: Oh! Sir, your suit looks damaged. Would you like a refund?
> A: Yes, please! Thank you so much, ma'am.
> C: Lily, we will talk about this later.
> B: I hate this job.

## 202. Something New

> Lin and Bea are standing together in the park.
> They're both holding skateboards and wearing helmets. Kids are skating around them.
> A: Why are we doing this again?
> B: Because I've always wanted to try skateboarding.
> B: I try to do one new thing every day!
> A: OK, that's why you are trying skateboarding.
> A: But why am I doing it?
> B: Because you're my friend and you support me!
> B: Don't worry, it'll be fun!
> A: But don't you think we're too old for skateboarding?
> B: Excuse me. We are not old!
> A: We're at least ten years older than everyone here.
> B: Oh, Lin, watch out!
> An 8-year-old girl skates past Lin.
> C: Excuse me, ma'am!
> A: Did that little girl just call me "ma'am"?
> Bea laughs at Lin.
> B: Just get on your skateboard and try it.
> B: If you fall, I promise I'll catch you!
> A: Fine. I'll try it.
> Lin gets on the skateboard and immediately falls off.
> A: You promised to catch me!
> B: I'm sorry. I didn't expect you to fall right away.
> Bea helps Lin stand up.
> B: Come on. Let's go catch that girl who called you "ma'am."
> Later that day, Lin and Bea are at the hospital.
> Bea's arm is broken.
> B: Maybe skateboarding was a bad idea. I just really like to do one new thing every day.
> A: Well, have you ever broken your arm before?
> B: No…
> A: Then you did two new things today!

## 203. The Lost Costume

> Lily is helping Zari get ready for the school play.
> A: Where's my costume?! I need to be on the stage in five minutes, and I can't find it!
> B: You always lose things. Do you need help looking?
> A: Yes, please!
> Lily looks in the closet.
> B: I don't know what I'm looking for.
> A: My costume is a red dress. Please, we have to hurry!
> B: I don't see any dresses in here.
> A: I'm the main actor in the play! I can't go on the stage without my costume!
> Lily looks at the stage. The other actors have started their scene.
> B: Uh-oh… Zari, come here and look at Jenny's dress. Do you recognize it?
> A: Jenny is wearing my costume?! I don't understand. Did she take it on purpose?
> B: Maybe she was jealous because you got a bigger part in the play.
> Jenny smiles at Zari from the stage.
> A: What am I going to do?
> B: Well, I saw one costume you can use.
> A: Really? Where?
> Lily gets a new costume from the closet for Zari.
> A: No!
> B: It's the only other costume I could find.
> A: Fine. I'll go put it on.

> B: Wow, you're actually going to wear that?
> A: I'm going to be in this play, and Jenny is not going to stop me!
