> Lily sees Jenny walk off the stage. Jenny looks furious.
> C: I don't understand! The audience loves her!
> B: Yeah, you're right. Thanks for your help, Jenny.

## 204. The Cat Rule

> Eddy and Junior are taking care of a neighbor's cat. The cat is sleeping on Junior's lap.
> A: Junior, you need to wash the dishes.
> B: I can't do that now, Dad. It's the Cat Rule!
> A: What's the Cat Rule?
> B: If a cat is sleeping on your lap, you can't stand up to do anything.
> A: Hmm. I've never heard of the Cat Rule…
> B: So, Dad, can you bring me a drink?
> A: Can't you get it yourself?
> B: No! Cat Rule!
> A: Ugh, OK.
> Eddy puts a glass of juice on the table.
> B: Can you move the glass closer to me? I can't reach it because the cat is on my lap. Cat Rule!
> Eddy move the glass closer to Junior.
> B: And can you also also give me the remote control? I want to watch something on TV, but—
> A: The Cat Rule. Yeah, yeah, I know.
> Eddy leaves the room for a while, then he returns.
> A: Junior, when are you going to wash the dishes?
> B: I can't do anything until the cat wakes up!
> Eddy tries to move the cat.
> A: Hey, cat—
> B: Don't wake the cat up on purpose, Dad! That's mean!
> A: That cat has been sleeping for quite a while…
> B: He had a busy day.
> Someone knocks on the door.
> A: Do you want to answer the door? Oh right, you can't. Cat Rule, right?
> Eddy answers the door and comes back with a pizza.
> B: You ordered my favorite pizza!
> A: And now I'm going to eat the whole pizza by myself in the kitchen! I'd share with you, but you can't stand up. Cat Rule!

## 205. Don't Feed The Seals

> Lucy and her granddaughter, Lin, are visiting a beach. It is covered with hundreds of seals.
> They see a sign that says, "Danger! Do not feed the seals! $100 fine."
> A: Wow! I've never seen this many seals in my life.
> B: Why are those seals just lying there?
> A: They're at the beach. That's what we do at the beach.
> B: I still wish they would do something.
> A: You're not the only one. Look!
> Lucy points at a teenage boy throwing popcorn to the seals.
> Lucy shouts at the boy.
> A: Hey! You can't feed the seals!
> The boy shouts back at Lucy.
> C: Go away!
> The boy continues feeding the seals.
> A: He shouldn't have done that.
> A crowd of seals start to surround the boy.
> B: Oh no! The seals are chasing him!
> C: Help me! Please!
> A: We have to get their attention!
> A: Do you have anything you can throw?
> Lin looks in her bag.
> B: Just this sandwich.
> Lucy takes the sandwich from Lin and throws it toward the seals.
> A: Hey, seals! Look over here!
> B: It's working!
> A: It's working… too well.
> The seals begin moving toward Lin and Lucy.
> B: The seals are coming toward us!
> A: Run!
> Lin and Lucy turn and run into a park ranger.
> D: Excuse me.
> B: Help! Those seals are chasing us!
> D: Because you fed them!
> B: We weren't feeding them!
> D: I saw you throw that sandwich.
> A: We were trying to rescue the boy!
> D: What boy?
> Lin and Lucy turn and see the boy running away.
> D: It says on the sign, "Don't feed the seals." You need to pay a $100 fine.
> A: We should have let the seals eat the boy.

## 206. Yoga Class

> Lucy invited Eddy to a yoga class.
> They're in the studio getting ready.
> A: So, you've never been to a yoga class?
> B: No, but I'm excited to try!
> A: Maybe you should take the class for beginners instead…
> B: No way! I'm not a beginner. I exercise all the time!
> A: OK, but remember to go slow.
> A: Yoga is difficult.
> A: You need to control your breathing.
> B: Well, I already know how to breathe…
> The yoga instructor enters the studio.
> C: Good morning, everyone!
> C: Let's start by sitting down.
> B: This is easy…
> B: Also, that instructor is cute!
> A: Eddy, remember to be careful.
> B: Don't worry! I run every day. I'll be fine.
> C: Now, lift your left leg.
> Eddy starts to sweat.
> C: Sir, are you OK?
> B: Yes, yes. I'm fine!
> C: Good. OK, now when you're ready, lift your right leg.
> B: What? Lucy? How are you doing that?
> A: Just remember to breathe…
> C: Now, put your right leg in front of your left leg and lift your arms. Perfect…
> B: Lucy, this hurts…
> A: Breathe, Eddy!
> Several minutes later, Eddy wakes up. Lucy and the instructor are looking down at him.
> A: Eddy, are you OK?
> B: Uh, yeah, but… what happened?
> A: You fainted.
> C: And you were sweating… a lot.
> B: Sorry.
> C: Sir, was this your first time doing yoga?
> B: Uhh… yeah.
> C: I think you should come back tomorrow. We have a class for beginners… like you.

## 207. The Flu Shot

> Eddy and his son Junior are waiting in a small room at the doctor's office.
> A: I wish I didn't have to get a flu shot…
> B: I know! You must be scared, son.
> B: But this shot will keep you healthy!
> A: Will the shot hurt?
> B: It might hurt for a second, so you have to be very brave!
> A: But I don't know how to be brave!
> B: Just think about the warrior in your video game. He's not afraid of anything, right?
> A: That's right. He fights dragons!
> B: Exactly!
> A: OK. I'm going to be brave. I'm not going to scream or cry.
> There is a knock on the door. It's the doctor.
> C: Hello, Junior! Are you ready for your shot?
> A: Uh… I think so.
> The doctor opens the drawer and takes out a needle.
> A: Oh no, Dad, the needle is so big!
> B: Oh. Wow, you're right. That needle is very big.
> A: Doctor, I don't think I can do this!
> C: OK, Junior… I'll give your dad a flu shot first, so you can see it's very safe.
> B: What? I'm getting a flu shot?
> C: Why not?
> B: Because this appointment is for Junior, not for me.
> C: You should get a flu shot too.
> A: What's wrong, Dad? You don't look very good.
> B: That needle is very big!
> A: Dad, this shot will help you stay healthy. We have to be very brave, remember?
> B: Yes… Yes, I remember…
> The doctor gives Eddy his flu shot.
> B: Ow!
> The doctor puts the needle away.
> C: I'm finished! That was a good plan, Junior.
> B: What plan? Junior, I don't understand.
> A: Well, Dad, the Doctor and I just convinced you to get your flu shot!

## 208. Where's My Jacket？

> Oscar knocks on Eddy's door. Eddy opens it.
> A: Eddy, do you have the jacket I gave you last week?
> B: Your blue jacket? Don't you hate that jacket?
> A: I changed my mind. I really need it back now.
> B: Sorry, but I gave the jacket to Lin!
> A: What? Why?
> B: It didn't fit me.
> A: Oh no. Well, maybe Lin will give it back to me…
> B: Good luck!
> Oscar runs to Lin's apartment.
> A: Lin, Eddy told me he gave you my jacket…
> C: Yes! I loved it!
> A: Oh, good. Then you must still have it!
> C: No. I'm allergic to the material of the jacket. I gave it to Bea.
> A: Ugh! I need it back.
> C: I think Bea is home now.
> Oscar goes to Bea's apartment.
> D: Oscar! It's nice to see you!
> A: Hello, Bea. I need my blue jacket back. Lin said she gave it to you.
> D: Oh! I'm sorry, it was such a warm jacket… I thought someone who needs it should have it.
> D: I donated it to a store this morning.
> A: Oh no!
> D: They close in an hour, so you need to hurry!
> Oscar runs to the store. He gets there a few minutes before it closes. He talks to the clerk.
> A: Hi! I am wondering if you have any blue jackets.
> E: Oh! Actually, someone just donated one… here it is! It's only fifty dollars.
> A: Only fifty dollars?!
> E: Yes! It's a good deal. But we don't give refunds.
> A: That's fine. I'll buy it.
> Oscar gives her money and she puts the jacket into a bag.
> E: Also, that jacket has a cool secret pocket!
> A: You… found the secret pocket?
> E: Yes! And you won't believe this: I found $500 in it! I donated it to our charity. It's going to help a lot of people.
> A: That's… very kind.
> E: Well, enjoy your new jacket!
> Oscar gives the bag back to her.
> A: Actually, I don't need this jacket anymore. I think I'll donate it again.

## 209. Bad Monkey

> Eddy and Junior are looking at the monkeys at the zoo. Suddenly, Eddy hears Junior shout.
> A: Stop! Thief!
> B: Junior, what's wrong?
> A: That monkey stole the candy that I had in my pocket!
> B: Ha, ha, you have a great imagination! But a monkey didn't take your candy.
> A: He did take my candy. Look at him!
> The monkey smiles at Eddy.
> B: He looks like a happy monkey.
> A: Yeah, he's happy because he ate my candy.
> Eddy looks at his phone for a minute. The monkey throws a candy wrapper at Junior. Junior picks it up.
> B: Ha! If the monkey took your candy, then why do you have the wrapper?
> A: The monkey threw it at me! He wants me to get in trouble.
> The zookeeper walks over.
> C: Did this monkey do something to you?
> A: Yes! He stole my candy!
> C: Oh yes. He does that a lot.
> B: He does?
> C: Yes, he looks cute, but—ouch!
> The monkey is throwing rocks at the zookeeper's head. The monkey starts to laugh.
> C: He's the worst monkey that we've ever had at this zoo.
> A: I knew it!
> C: I hate this monkey.
> C: He did a terrible thing to my favorite hat.
> The zookeeper and the monkey look at each other. The monkey steals the zookeeper's hat and runs away.
> C: My hat! Not again!
> The zookeeper chases the monkey.
> A: Do you see, Dad? I wasn't lying.
> B: Wow, I'm sorry that I didn't believe you, Junior. I'll buy you some more candy.
> Eddy looks for his wallet.
> B: That's strange… I can't find my wallet.
> A: I think I know who took it…

## 210. The List

> Bea and Lin are taking a trip in Bea's car. Bea is driving.
> A: Hey! Can we stop at that amusement park?
> B: Sorry, we can't go there. It's not on the list.
> A: What list?
> Bea hands Lin a piece of paper.
> B: I made a list of all the things we're going to do on the trip!
> B: "Stop at the lake, take photos of the mountain, eat lunch at the vegetarian restaurant…"
> A: What if we want to stop somewhere that's not on the list?
> B: We won't need to stop anywhere else. All of the best places are on my list!
> Lin turns on the radio.
> B: Oh! We don't need the radio! I brought the perfect music for driving.
> Bea connects her phone to the car.
> B: I picked out the best three hundred and two songs for driving in the countryside.
> They drive past a sign for fresh berries.
> A: Let's buy some berries!
> B: That's not on the list.
> Lin points out the window.
> A: Oh, look! An ice cream shop! Let's stop!
> B: Maybe on the way home…
> B: Right now, we only have time to stop at the places on the list.
> Lin takes Bea's list and throws it out the window.
> B: My list!
> A: Now we can stop anywhere.
> Bea stops the car and then turns it around.
> B: I can't believe you did that! We need to go back and get the list.
> Suddenly, the vehicle stops in the middle of the road.
> A: What's happening?
> B: We ran out of gas!
> A: Maybe next time we should add "gas station" to the list.

## 211. Monster Under the Bed

> It's late at night. Junior is in his bed, but he can't sleep.
> A: Dad! There's a monster under my bed! I need you!
> Eddy runs to Junior's bedroom.
> B: It's OK, Junior. Let me look. If I see a monster, then I'll make him leave.
> A: Thanks, Dad.
> Eddy looks under the bed.
> B: I don't see any monsters, so it's safe to go to sleep.
> A: I can't sleep! Maybe the monster is hiding!
> Eddy starts to crawl under the bed.
> B: There isn't a lot of space down here. I don't know if I'll fit, Junior.
> A: Please! I'm scared!
> Eddy crawls further under the bed.
> B: Hello? Monster? Are you hiding?
> B: No, Junior, the monster is gone!
> A: Thanks, Dad.
> Eddy tries to crawl out from under the bed.
> B: Um… Junior? I think I'm stuck.
> A: Uh-oh. Let me help you!
> Junior tries to lift the bed.
> A: Ugh… the bed is too heavy! Let me try to pull you out.
> Junior pulls Eddy's legs.
> A: Oh no, Dad… you're really stuck!
> B: Can you pull harder?
> A: This is hard work. I'm tired.
> A: I'm going to lie down, OK?
> B: Maybe if I move my head, then I can get out…
> B: Or maybe if I turn my shoulders…
> B: I think it's working! Junior, can you reach my legs and pull?
> B: Junior? Junior?
> Junior has fallen asleep. He begins to snore.
> B: Ah. OK.
> B: I'll just sleep here…
> Eddy closes his eyes.
> B: Goodnight, Junior.

## 212. Cousins

> Lily and her mom are standing outside Lily's aunt's house.
> A: Lily, please be nice to your cousin Jessica tonight. She's really excited to see you!
> B: I'm not excited to see Jessica.
> A: Why?! She's so smart, talented, and polite…
> B: I know. She's so annoying.
> A: Lily. We're going inside.
> They walk into the house.
> B: Hi, Aunt Mindy. Hello, Jessica.
> C: Hi, Lily!
> D: How's school going, Lily? Jessica is taking an advanced science class. She's studying climate change.
> B: Great.
> A: Well, Lily is a drummer in a band.
> D: Oh? Jessica is in the orchestra at her school. They're playing for the Queen of Spain next month.
> A: The Queen?
> D: She also won several trophies. Jessica, why don't you show Lily your trophies?
> C: Sure!
> B: Ugh. Fine.
> Lily follows Jessica to her bedroom, and Jessica closes the door.
> C: Come on, let's go.
> C: We can climb down the balcony.
> B: What?!
> C: We've got an hour before dinner! They won't know that we left. My neighbor is having a party, and his hip-hop group is performing.
> B: OK…
> Later, at the party…
> B: Wow, Jessica. I did not expect you to be so cool.
> C: I know.
> Lily's phone rings. It's her mom.
> A: Lily, where are you? What did you do to Jessica?
> B: What did I do?
> Jessica takes the phone.
> C: Hello! It's Jessica. Lily and I are at a… classical music concert.
> A: Oh!
> C: I'm teaching Lily about my favorite composer.
> A: You're such a good cousin, Jessica.
> C: Aw, thanks!
> Jessica gives the phone back to Lily.
> B: Hi, Mom. So I'm not in trouble?
> A: Of course not!
> A: Lily, you could learn a lot from your cousin.
> B: Actually, I think you're right.

## 213. Inhale, Exhale

> Oscar is lying on the sofa at his therapist's office. The therapist is taking notes.
> A: So, how are you feeling today?
> B: I am feeling stressed!
> The therapist nods her head.
> A: And what is making you feel stressed?
> B: Everything! Don't you watch the news?!
> A: OK. Try to stay calm. Inhale slowly and then exhale.
> Oscar inhales and then exhales. He shakes his head.
> B: No. This isn't helping! I don't like hearing myself breathe.
> A: I see. Then, what is something that helps you feel calm?
> B: I don't ever feel calm.
> The therapist smiles patiently.
> A: You could try to meditate.
> B: No. I don't have time to sit and do nothing!
> A: Maybe you need something more active. Have you tried yoga?
> B: Yes. But I hate the music yoga teachers play. And anyway, I can't touch my toes!
> The therapist takes a deep breath.
> A: You could take a long, hot bath to relax…
> B: By the time I relax, the water is always cold!
> A: OK. Try to stay calm. Inhale, exhale.
> Oscar's therapist tries one more suggestion.
> A: You could go to the beach.
> A: Everyone likes a little bit of sun.
> B: Not me! The last time I went to the beach, I got a sunburn and all of my students called me "Mr. Tomato!"
> B: I hate being called Mr. Tomato!
> A: Oscar! You're shouting again!
> She puts her notebook down.
> A: I think I know something that will help you feel more relaxed.
> Oscar and his therapist walk outside. They count to three, and then they both scream loudly.
> A: Ah!
> B: Ah!
> B: You're right! I do feel more relaxed now.
> A: I do, too.

## 214. Front Row

> Eddy is on a date with Rose. They go to see a comedy show.
> A: Let's sit in the front row!
> B: Sure!
> A: Marie Baker is the funniest comedian. She always makes jokes about the audience!
> B: Marie Baker? Uh-oh.
> B: Um, can we sit in the back row instead? Those seats look better.
> A: These are great seats!
> Marie comes to the stage and looks into the audience.
> C: How's everyone tonight?
> C: I see a beautiful elderly couple… Thanks for coming out past your bedtime!
> The couple laughs.
> C: And I see a man in running shorts. Did you get lost on your way to the gym?
> A: She's talking about you!
> C: Tell me, miss, does your husband lift weights while he's sleeping?
> A: Haha, this is only our second date!
> Eddy looks uncomfortable.
> C: He's wearing those old sneakers on your second date?! Please don't tell me there's going to be a third date.
> Rose laughs. Eddy doesn't.
> Later, Eddy and Rose see Marie at the bar.
> Eddy tries to hide his face with Rose's scarf.
> A: What are you doing?
> B: My face is cold.
> C: Oh, look! It's Eddy, the gym teacher.
> A: Wait, do you know each other?
> C: We met at a bar a long time ago.
> C: Eddy asked for my number, but he never called me.
> B: I wrote your number on my hand. But then my hand got sweaty… and I lost the number.
> A: Why didn't you save her number in your phone?
> B: Because… I wrote it on my hand.
> C: Oh, that's hilarious. I'm going to use that in my next show.
> Marie walks away laughing.
> A: Wow! You inspired Marie Baker's next joke! You're going to be famous!
> B: Great.

## 215. Eddy's Night Out

> Eddy puts on a tie. His son Junior watches.
> A: I'm so excited to stay at my friend's house tonight! But won't you be bored without me?
> B: No, I'm going on a date!
> B: It'll be nice to eat something besides pizza for dinner… and to watch a serious movie instead of cartoons.
> A: That sounds boring.
> Junior leaves. Eddy gets a text.
> B: Oh no, my date is cancelled!
> B: Hmm, I still want to do something tonight.
> A few minutes later, Eddy is at Oscar's house.
> B: Thanks for inviting me to your house!
> C: I didn't invite you here. You just came over.
> C: But since you're already here, you can stay for a snack. I'm having cheese and caviar.
> B: Ooh, that sounds fancy!
> Eddy tries some cheese.
> B: Um, why does it… smell so bad?
> C: You don't like it? Try the caviar.
> Eddy eats some caviar. He coughs and drinks some water.
> B: Cough, cough! Wow, that… tastes like the ocean.
> C: You hate it, don't you?
> B: I hate it… so much.
> C: Well, I'm going to paint now, so please leave.
> B: OK, goodnight!
> Eddy goes to Bea's apartment.
> B: Hi, Bea! Do you want to do something?
> D: I'm going to a film festival. You should come!
> They go to the movie theater.
> B: What kind of movie are we watching? I hope it's a romantic comedy!
> D: It's an international art film.
> B: That sounds interesting!
> D: It's about death, and it's four hours long!
> B: Oh…
> They sit and watch the film.
> D: Eddy, are you enjoying the movie?
> D: Eddy?
> Eddy has fallen asleep.
> The next morning, Junior comes home.
> B: Junior! You're home!
> B: Let's watch cartoons and order pizza! Doesn't that sound fun?
> A: You were bored without me, weren't you?

## 216. Checking In

> Bea runs through the airport. She is carrying a heavy suitcase and trying to get through the crowd.
> A: Excuse me! Sorry, I'm late!
> Bea arrives at the check-in desk.
> A: Hello! Can I still check in for my flight?
> B: Maybe. Where are you going?
> A: Hawaii! I'm so excited! My friends are getting married!
> B: That's wonderful. You have fifteen minutes. You can still get on the flight.
> A: Great! Whew, I'm not usually late!
> A: I just have to check this bag.
> B: I'm sorry. It's too late to check your bag.
> A: What? You just said I can still get on my flight!
> B: You can. But not your bag.
> A: But I need to be on this flight!
> B: Sorry. Those are the rules.
> A: Ugh! I can't miss this wedding!
> B: Maybe your friends will take some good pictures.
> Bea takes a deep breath. Then she gets an idea.
> A: If I can't check a bag, then I won't check a bag.
> B: Finally, you understand.
> Bea opens up her suitcase.
> B: Excuse me, ma'am?
> Bea puts on a swimsuit over her outfit. Then she puts on another one.
> A: Ugh, why did I pack so many swimsuits?!
> B: What are you doing?
> A: I'm going to wear all of my clothes on the plane.
> A: There are no rules about that, right?
> Next, Bea puts on two shirts, a pair of jeans, a formal dress, and an enormous hat. Her suitcase is now empty.
> B: You still can't take that suitcase on the plane.
> A: It's OK. You can keep it.
> B: Is there anything else I can help you with?
> A: Can you get me a ride to the gate? I can't move.

## 217. Bad at Soccer

> Junior is in his room playing a video game. Eddy comes in with a shopping bag.
> A: Junior! Look! I bought something for you! A new soccer ball!
> B: Dad, you know I'm bad at soccer.
> A: That's not true! You're good at everything.
> B: We played soccer in gym class, and I was not good.
> A: I don't believe you're not good. Come on, I'll show you how to kick the ball.
> Eddy and Junior go outside to the patio.
> A: It's a perfect day for soccer!
> B: It's also a perfect day for the air conditioner. It's really hot out here!
> Eddy kicks the ball to Junior. Junior tries to kick it back, but he misses.
> B: See? I told you I'm not good at soccer.
> A: Try one more time! And kick the ball as hard as you can!
> Eddy kicks the ball to Junior again. This time, Junior kicks it as hard as he can.
> B: I kicked the ball!
> The ball flies high through the air.
> A: I knew you were good at soccer!
> Suddenly, they hear a loud crash.
> A: Oh no. The ball broke Lucy's window!
> Lucy comes outside holding the soccer ball.
> A: Lucy? Hi! Uh… You look upset.
> C: Of course I'm upset. You guys broke my window!
> A: Junior, tell Lucy you're sorry.
> B: Me?! But this was your idea!
> A: Junior…
> B: Fine.
> B: Lucy, I'm sorry that my dad made me play soccer.

## 218. What's the Recipe？

> Vikram walks into a bakery.
> A: Hi. My wife loves your apple pastries.
> B: Cool.
> A: I bake, too, but she says your pastries are better than anything I make.
> A: Could you give me the recipe?
> B: Absolutely not! My recipes are secret.
> A: Ah, I'm sorry that I asked.
> B: There's a line. Are you going to buy anything?
> A: Yes. One box of apple pastries.
> B: A whole box? You're trying to guess my recipe!
> A: I'm sorry, I just have to know how to make them!
> B: Please leave my store. And don't come back.
> Vikram looks shocked.
> The next day, Bea nervously walks into the bakery.
> C: Uh, I would like…
> B: Yes?
> C: One box of apple pastries.
> Bea looks out the window, where Vikram is waiting.
> The baker sees Vikram.
> B: It's that guy! You're helping him steal my recipe. Get out!
> Bea runs out of the store.
> C: I'm sorry, Vikram. I'm bad at lying.
> A: It's fine.
> C: But how will you get the recipe?
> A: I have a new plan.
> One week later, Vikram walks into the bakery. He's holding a plate with an apple pastry on it.
> B: It's you again! I told you not to come back!
> A: I spent the whole week baking.
> B: Were you trying to make my recipe?
> A: Not exactly. Try one bite, and then I'll leave.
> B: Fine.
> The baker takes a bite of Vikram's pastry.
> B: This doesn't taste like my apple pastry.
> A: No.
> B: It tastes better.
> A: Thank you. My wife thinks so, too. And I'd like to give you the recipe.
> B: Really? Why?
> A: Because I believe good recipes should always be shared.

## 219. On the News

> Zari and Lily are watching the news on TV.
> A reporter is interviewing a woman who rescued a boy from a lake.
> A: I wish I could be on the news.
> B: Really? I would hate all that attention.
> A: I wouldn't! I would be a great hero.
> B: That sounds like a nightmare to me.
> A: I have an idea! We should rescue someone.
> B: You rescue. I'll watch.
> Zari and Lily walk around the neighborhood.
> A: I'm going to help that man cross the street.
> B: Why? There are no cars coming.
> Zari runs to help the man.
> A: Excuse me, sir. Can I help you cross this busy street?
> C: What? I don't need help!
> A: But I thought older people need help crossing the street…
> C: I'm only forty-five!
> Zari runs back to Lily.
> B: Well, that was a bad idea.
> A: You're right.
> A: Let's find a burning building and I'll rescue someone.
> B: Maybe we should go home before you get hurt.
> A: I could rescue a cat from a tree…
> B: What cat?
> A: That cat.
> Zari points at a cat resting on the sidewalk.
> B: That cat is not in a tree.
> A: Not yet.
> Zari grabs the cat and starts climbing a tree.
> B: Zari, this is a terrible idea.
> Later, Junior is at his home watching the news on TV.
> D: Dad, look! A reporter is interviewing my babysitter, Zari!
> E: I've climbed up this tree to talk to this embarrassed young girl.
> E: Now, you said you were trying to rescue a cat… but where's the cat?
> A: Uh, the cat climbed down. And I got stuck in the tree.
> D: Wow! I guess it's pretty easy to get on the news.

## 220. Save the Animals!

> Oscar is walking into the school where he works. He's wearing a long fur coat. Another teacher stops him.
> A: Oscar, wait! Are you wearing a fur coat?
> B: Yes, isn't it gorgeous? It belonged to my uncle. Fur coats were very fashionable when he was young.
> A: Uh… yes, but I don't know if it's still OK to wear a fur coat. Especially not today, because—
> B: Oh, Paul! You don't know anything about fashion.
> Oscar and Paul get to the school building and see kids in front of a sign that says: "Save the animals!"
> B: What's this?
> A: This is what I was trying to tell you… The kids are protesting to save the animals from the fur industry.
> Lily walks over holding a bucket of red paint.
> C: The fur industry is cruel! Take off that coat, or I'm going to throw this paint on you.
> B: This coat is vintage! It was my uncle's! I didn't hurt any animals!
> C: Yes, but your uncle did. Take it off.
> B: It's cold right now! And this is the warmest coat I have!
> C: You want to hurt animals so you can be warm and stylish?
> Oscar turns to Paul.
> B: See, Paul? I told you this coat was stylish.
> C: I know you're my art teacher, but I have to do this.
> Lily holds up the bucket of paint.
> B: Wait!
> B: My coat isn't real fur.
> C: It isn't?
> A: Why didn't you just say that?
> B: I wanted everyone to think I was wearing an expensive fur coat.
> C: Oh. In that case, you can have this paint back. I stole it from your classroom.

## 221. Junior's New Business

> Eddy comes home from work. His son Junior is excitedly waiting for him.
> A: Dad, look what I got!
> Junior proudly shows his dad a new video game.
> B: The new Space Viking game? Where did you get the money for that?
> A: From my new business. I'm cleaning windows in the neighborhood. My first customer was Bea!
> A: I love having my own business. The pay is great!
> B: Wow, I'm impressed. I bet you worked really hard!
> A: Yeah, I'm tired! Can we play my game now?
> The next morning, on his way to work, Eddy notices that his neighbor Bea's windows are extremely dirty.
> Eddy goes back into the building and knocks on Bea's door.
> C: Oh, hi, Eddy!
> B: Bea, did Junior clean your windows?
> C: Well… I paid him ten dollars, but he hasn't washed them yet.
> B: Oh no. I'm so sorry.
> C: It's OK. He's just a kid. But the other neighbors are pretty upset.
> B: Other neighbors? How many others?
> When Junior gets home from school, his father is waiting for him.
> A: Is something wrong, Dad?
> B: Yes. I was late for work today because I spent the morning cleaning windows.
> A: Are you starting a window cleaning business too?
> B: No. I was cleaning the windows you promised to clean. Why did you take money without doing the work?
> A: I tried to clean the window, but I'm not tall enough to reach them!
> A: But I'm growing, so I should be able to reach them soon.
> B: Oh, Junior.
> Junior walks back outside.
> A: Wow, Dad, you really did a great job on all those windows. They're perfect and shiny now!
> B: Yes, I know.
> A: Would you like to be my new business partner?

## 222. Too Much Stuff

> Lin comes home. Her grandmother Lucy's belongings are all over the living room.
> A: What's going on? This place is really messy.
> B: Sorry, my cousin Mae is coming to visit. You know how she's so neat and organized…
> A: And she thinks you have too much stuff.
> B: I know! I want to impress her by getting rid of some stuff.
> A: OK, let me help.
> B: Lin, you're the messiest person I know!
> A: But I just watched a documentary about an organization expert. I know what I'm talking about.
> A: First, you have to organize your belongings…
> B: That's obvious, and I already did that.
> Lucy points to three piles of stuff.
> B: That pile is stuff that I want to keep.
> B: That pile is stuff that I don't want to throw out.
> B: And that pile is stuff that I love.
> A: But you're not throwing away anything! You're doing it wrong.
> Several hours later, Lin and Lucy have finished reorganizing Lucy's belongings.
> Lin proudly points at the new piles.
> A: These are items that you use every day.
> A: These items bring you happiness.
> A: These items are important to you.
> B: And we found one thing to throw out…
> A: Yes! This ugly goat sculpture!
> B: That's fine. I don't even know where it came from.
> Lin puts the goat sculpture in the trash.
> The doorbell rings. It's Lucy's cousin, Mae. Lucy invites her in.
> C: Wow, the place looks so much neater than the last time I visited.
> B: I'm so glad you like it!
> C: But where's that gorgeous goat sculpture I gave you?

## 223. Secret Place

> Zari and Lily are hanging out on the roof of their apartment building.
> A: It's so cool up here. Why don't we ever come to the roof?
> They notice a large cardboard box making noise.
> B: What is that?
> Zari looks inside the box and sees Junior playing a video game.
> A: Junior, what are you doing in this box?
> C: Hi. This is my secret place. I come here to be by myself.
> A: Cool!
> C: Thanks, but please don't tell anyone about it.
> B: We won't.
> The next day, Junior goes back to his secret place on the roof, but Lily and Zari are already there.
> B: Hi Junior! Look, we brought some lights and decorations.
> A: This place is even cooler now.
> C: But it's not secret anymore.
> D: Hello? I heard footsteps up here.
> Their neighbor Bea joins them.
> D: Whoa, what is this?
> C: This used to be my favorite place.
> D: Wow, there's a great view up here.
> D: I have an extra couch.
> D: Should I bring it up?
> A: Definitely. Is that OK, Junior?
> C: Fine, but no one else can know about this place.
> The next day when Junior goes to the roof, he hears music and voices.
> Lily, Zari, and Bea are hanging out on the roof with a bunch of their neighbors, including Lucy and Eddy.
> C: Dad?
> E: Junior! I'm so glad you're here! This is where everyone hangs out now!
> F: Hi Junior! We're going to have a dance party! Come join us!
> C: That's OK, I'm going to go now.
> E: Where?
> C: Ahhh… To find a new secret place.

## 224. Eddy's Tears

> Vikram is stirring a pot of soup at the stove while his friend Eddy cuts vegetables next to him.
> A: How was your date with Mira last night?
> B: I thought it was amazing, but now I don't know. I think she might break up with me.
> Eddy gives Vikram a bowl of carrots. Vikram adds them to the pot.
> A: Really? What did she say?
> B: She wants me to be more sensitive.
> A: Oh, you can definitely do that! Cut this into slices, please.
> Vikram gives Eddy a potato.
> B: I'm trying to be more sensitive, but it's very hard.
> A: Have you tried writing in a journal?
> B: Yes, I did!
> A: How was it?
> B: I fell asleep.
> A: Hmm, OK. Have you tried talking to a therapist?
> Eddy gives Vikram a bowl of potatoes. Vikram adds them to the pot.
> B: Yes, I did.
> A: And?
> B: The therapist fell asleep.
> A: I see. Can you cut these onions?
> B: Sure. I really like Mira. I don't want her to break up with me.
> Eddy's eyes begin to fill with tears.
> A: Eddy! Look at you! You're being more sensitive!
> Eddy wipes the tears out of his eyes.
> A: You just need to talk about how you feel more often!
> B: No, I think I just need to cut onions when I'm with Mira!
> Eddy puts two onions in his pocket.
> B: Can I keep these?

## 225. I'm Fine!

> Lucy broke her arm while she was rock climbing. She is wearing a cast.
> Lucy's granddaughter, Lin, hired a nurse to help her at home.
> A: I told you that I don't need a nurse!
> B: It's just for a few days, while you recover.
> A: I'm fine! Have fun on your trip!
> C: Don't worry, I'll take good care of you.
> A: I don't need help. Go babysit someone else!
> B: Grandma! Please, just let him help.
> Lin leaves Lucy with the nurse, Gilberto. Lucy ignores him and walks outside.
> Gilberto follows Lucy and immediately sees her climbing up an old ladder to pick some oranges from a tree.
> C: Lucy, you can't climb a ladder!
> C: You just had an operation!
> A: I'm fine! I just wanted to make some fresh orange juice.
> Lucy goes into the dining room and puts the oranges in a bowl.
> A: Hmm. I think this table would look better by the window.
> C: Wait!
> Lucy pushes the heavy table across the room. Gilberto runs over to her.
> C: You really should let me help you. You don't want to hurt yourself again!
> A: I didn't need any help.
> C: The doctor said you need to rest.
> A: I'm full of energy! I'm going to make us lunch now.
> C: If you're not going to listen to me, then I'm going outside.
> Gilberto exits.
> A: Finally, he's gone!
> Lucy grabs a jar of pickled vegetables.
> And tries to open it.
> A: Ugh. How can I do this with one hand?
> Lucy tries again, but she can't open the jar.
> A: Uh… Gilberto?
> Gilberto returns and sees Lucy with the jar. He smiles.
> C: Hello, Lucy. Is there something you would like to say to me?
> A: Yes… I need your help.

## 226. Surprise Party

> Lily and Zari see Vikram buying balloons in a store.
> A: Hi, Vikram. Nice balloons!
> B: Thanks, it's my wife's birthday. I'm having a surprise party for her.
> A: But Priti is here!
> C: We just saw her in the store.
> B: Oh no! She left work early? If she sees me, the party won't be a surprise.
> B: Can you distract Priti?
> B: I need to go home and set up the party.
> C: Sure, we'll help you.
> Zari and Lily find Priti holding a bottle of shampoo.
> C: Hi Priti! Do you use that shampoo?
> D: Oh, hi! Yes, I do.
> C: I heard that it has dangerous chemicals in it.
> D: But it's organic.
> C: You should read the ingredients.
> A: Yeah, and you should look up all the ingredients on your phone… right now.
> D: I don't have time for that. I'm going home.
> Priti walks away.
> A: She can't go home yet! Vikram needs more time.
> Priti walks out of the store. Lily and Zari quickly run over to her. Lily is holding a wallet.
> C: Priti! You dropped your wallet.
> D: That's not mine.
> A: Uh… she meant your keys!
> Zari pulls keys out of her pocket.
> D: Those aren't my keys.
> Priti tries to walk away, and Zari runs in front of her and falls on the ground.
> A: Ow!
> D: Zari, are you OK?
> A: No, I feel really sick!
> Zari pretends to faint.
> C: Oh no. Please help her.
> Priti looks at Zari and Lily. She thinks for a moment.
> D: OK. I'll call an ambulance.
> Zari sits up.
> A: Don't call an ambulance!
> C: Look, she's feeling better now.
> D: OK, you're both being silly, and I don't have time.
> D: My husband is having a surprise party for me, and I can't be late.

## 227. The Principal's Office

> Eddy is sitting across from Principal Williams at his son Junior's school.
> A: Usually, Junior is a perfect student. He's smart, kind, and polite. But recently, he has been misbehaving.
> B: Oh no, what did he do now?
> A: He released a pigeon in the cafeteria.
> B: Where did he get a pigeon?
> A: And last week, he took apart the science teacher's chair.
> B: Wow! I didn't know he could do that.
> A: And the week before that, he filled my office with balloons.
> B: That probably took hours!
> A: Is everything OK at home?
> B: I thought so, until now.
> A: Why don't we talk to him together?
> Junior enters the office and sits down.
> A: Junior, we are both very worried about you.
> C: That's one thing you have in common!
> C: Also, you both like Italian food and soccer.
> C: Sorry that you're missing the big soccer game on TV right now, Dad.
> B: I really wanted to watch that game.
> A: I did too.
> C: Do you guys want to talk about soccer alone? Should I leave?
> A: Junior, we need to talk about your behavior at school.
> C: You can do that without me. And then you can talk about everything else that you have in common, like being single.
> B: Why does it matter that we're both single?
> A: I think I know what's going on.
> A: Junior, are you getting in trouble on purpose because you want me to date your father?
> C: Of course! You both love to punish me, so you should be together!

## 228. Is She Mad at Me？

> Lily and Zari are eating lunch at school. Zari stares at her phone.
> A: This is awful. I texted Maggie to ask if she wanted to hang out this weekend, but she's ignoring me.
> B: Wait. I thought we were hanging out this weekend. We're going to a concert.
> A: I want Maggie to come too!
> B: The last time we went to a concert with her, she sang louder than the band!
> A: Lily, don't be mean. Why hasn't Maggie texted me back? Is she mad at me?
> B: Why would anyone be mad at you?
> A: Maybe it's because we wore the same sweater yesterday.
> B: Even I have that sweater.
> A: Or maybe it's because I got a better grade than her in math class?
> B: You get better grades than everybody.
> A: Oh no! There she is.
> Zari stands up and nervously waves at Maggie. Maggie looks away.
> A: Did you see that? She is mad at me!
> B: Wow, I think you're right…
> Lily angrily walks over to Maggie.
> Maggie tries to hide her face with a textbook.
> B: Uhh… I can still see you.
> C: Hi, Lily.
> B: Why are you ignoring Zari?
> C: I'm not ignoring her…
> B: But Zari said you haven't texted her back.
> C: Yeah, because… I don't want to hang out with you.
> B: Wait, you haven't been hanging out with Zari because of me?
> C: Yes. You're always so mean.
> B: Oh… sorry…
> B: Please come to the concert.
> B: Zari and I both want you to come.
> C: Really? Great! We're going to have so much fun singing every song!
> B: Great…
> Lily walks back to Zari.
> A: What did she say?! Was she mad at me?
> B: Uh… yeah, but don't worry. I fixed everything.

## 229. The Best Cookies

> Junior and Eddy are in Vikram's kitchen.
> A: It's so great that you're letting us try new cookie recipes for your bakery.
> B: And when your bakery opens, we'll have free cookies for the rest of our lives!
> C: Let me get my notebook, and then you can try the cookies.
> Vikram leaves. Eddy and Junior look at a plate of cookies on the table.
> A: They look so good. Maybe we should try one now.
> B: Vikram told us to wait!
> A: But they're probably still warm…
> B: I guess we could try a very small bite…
> Junior grabs one of the cookies, takes a bite, and immediately spits it out.
> B: Yuck! This cookie is terrible!
> A: Vikram is an amazing baker. You probably picked a bad cookie.
> Eddy takes a bite of a cookie.
> A: Hmm. It's kind of dry and hard.
> Eddy tastes another cookie.
> A: They definitely have a unique flavor.
> B: Did he forget to add the sugar?
> A: Junior, we have to tell Vikram that we like these cookies.
> B: I thought you said we should always be honest!
> A: If we tell him how weird these cookies are, he'll feel really bad.
> Vikram comes back into the kitchen.
> C: Are you ready to try my cookies?
> A: We already tried them! They're so good!
> B: And now we have to go!
> C: But… the cookies are still in the oven.
> Vikram goes to the oven and takes out a pan of cookies.
> A: We ate the cookies that were on the table!
> C: The ones shaped like bones? Those are dog treats.
> B: We ate dog food?!
> A: Oh, these are pretty good for dog treats! I'm impressed!
> B: I think I'm going to be sick.

## 230. Dating‌ ‌Apps‌

> Eddy and his neighbor, Bea, are watching a movie.
> A: Ahhh… I want my life to be like a romantic comedy.
> B: So, you want a woman to fall in love with you after you spill coffee on her? That's not realistic.
> A: Yeah, you're right. I'm going to be alone forever!
> B: Come on, Eddy, that's not true!
> B: Have you tried a dating app?
> A: They don't work for me. I always forget my password.
> B: Eddy, how are you this bad with technology!?
> Bea grabs Eddy's phone.
> B: Here. I set up a profile on the dating app for you. Your password is "password."
> A: Why did you write that I like sports, romantic comedies, and spending time with my son?
> B: Because it's true!
> A: I sound like a boring person.
> Just then, Eddy's phone beeps.
> A: I have a match already!
> Eddy's phone beeps twelve more times.
> B: Whoa! You have a lot of matches.
> The next morning, Bea comes over to Eddy's apartment.
> B: Good morning, neighbor! I brought you coffee!
> Eddy says nothing. He is quickly typing on his phone.
> B: Are you talking to one of your matches on the app?
> A: Yes… well, I'm talking to… a few of them.
> B: Wait, are you wearing the same clothes from yesterday? You look exhausted!
> A: I've been awake all night!
> B: What? Why?
> A: This dating app! Women keep messaging me!
> Bea looks at Eddy's phone.
> B: Wait, you're messaging ninety-eight women? Did you accept every request? You have to say no to some of them!
> A: But any one of these women could be my soulmate. And… I wouldn't want to hurt anyone's feelings.
> Bea takes Eddy's phone away.
> B: You're too nice for dating apps, Eddy.

## 231. My Horse Hates Me

> Zari and Lily are at a farm in the countryside.
> A: I can't believe we're going to ride horses. I think I'm allergic to them.
> B: It'll be fun. Horses are magical creatures!
> A: Horses are dangerous animals, and you can't trust them.
> B: I've heard that if you look into a horse's eyes, then you can see the future.
> A: Why are we friends?
> Zari ignores Lily and points to a white horse.
> B: I want that one!
> C: That horse is very challenging.
> B: I love challenges!
> B: Lily, you should ride the black one! She's so pretty!
> C: I must warn you. That horse is very old, and she doesn't have a lot of energy.
> A: Perfect.
> Zari gets on the white horse, and he immediately starts running away from the farm.
> B: Stop! Please, stop!
> The horse suddenly stops, and Zari almost falls off.
> B: This horse is trying to kill me!
> Lily rides her horse over to Zari.
> A: I don't think you're doing it right.
> B: He's crazy. I can't control him!
> A: My horse is so calm. I think we have a special connection.
> B: You have a connection already?
> A: Are you jealous?
> B: No! I just need to spend more time with my horse…
> A: Ah-choo!
> Lily sneezes, and Zari's horse jumps.
> Zari falls into a puddle of water.
> B: My horse hates me! I give up.
> A: Mine is pretty cool. She lets me hug her.
> Lily leans forward and hugs her horse.
> A: I think I like horses more than people.
> Lily rides away. Zari looks into her horse's eyes.
> B: Oh no, I can see my future.
> B: I think I'm going to have a difficult ride back to the farm.

## 232. The Videotape

> Eddy brings his son, Junior, home from school.
> A: How was school today?
> B: Terrible! The teacher gave me a big part in a play.
> A: That's great!
> B: No! I'm very nervous!
> A: Acting is easy! I was the star of a play when I was your age.
> A: I was nervous, too. But it was fun!
> B: I don't know…
> A: It was recorded on videotape. Do you want to watch it?
> B: Sure! What's a videotape?
> Eddy searches in the closet.
> A: Here, this is a videotape!
> B: How do we turn it on?
> A: Ha ha, you watch it with a VCR!
> A: But I don't have one.
> Eddy and Junior go to Lucy's apartment.
> A: Lucy, do you have a VCR?
> C: No. I watch movies on my laptop, like a normal person.
> A: We want to watch a play I was in.
> B: My dad was the star!
> C: Ha, I want to see that. Let's ask Bea.
> Eddy, Junior, and Lucy go to Bea's apartment.
> A: Bea, you make videos! Can you play this videotape?
> D: Hmm… I don't have a VCR, but Lily might. She loves old movies.
> They go to Lily's apartment.
> D: Lily, do you have a VCR?
> C: We want to watch this videotape of Eddy in a school play.
> E: Of course. Old technology is cool. Also, that sounds hilarious.
> They sit down in Lily's living room and watch the videotape.
> A: That's me!
> C: Is that you singing?
> A: No. I'm behind the kid who is singing!
> E: You're the kid wearing the tree costume?
> A: Yeah.
> D: But you said you were the star.
> A: I felt like I was.
> C: What part do you have in your play, Junior?
> B: I'm playing a rock.
> A: Awesome! My son's going to be a star!

## 234. Tiny Hat

> Her guest, Lin, arrives wearing torn jeans and an old sweater.

> B: This is my cool outfit.

> A: Because you're my guest, and I came here to impress the fashion designer Mona Ma!
> B: That's why you're wearing a tiny hat?
> A: If I interview Mona Ma, it will really help my career!
> A photographer approaches Bea and Lin.
> C: Excuse me, can I take your photo?

> Bea steps away from Lin and the photographer takes a photo.

## 235. The Mountain

> Junior sits in class on a Monday morning. Everyone takes out their notebooks.
> A: Who wants to read their essay about what they did this weekend?
> Junior raises his hand.
> B: I want to read my essay!
> Junior stands up and begins to read.
> B: On Saturday morning, I climbed an enormous mountain. I woke up very early. It was very cold…
> C: Which mountain?
> B: Please wait until I'm done to ask questions. Thank you.
> B: I was all alone, and it was still dark when I started to climb.
> D: Is this true?
> B: Yes, it's true, Andy. Be quiet.
> B: I climbed for an hour and then I sat down to rest. I could hear wild dogs barking nearby. I was scared they were going to find me and eat me.
> D: You really climbed for an hour?
> B: I'm very athletic.
> B: I climbed so high that I started to feel weak. I was so hungry. I didn't have any food.
> B: I didn't have a phone to call for help.
> B: Just as I reached the top of the mountain, I fainted.
> A: Wow, Junior. This is an incredible story. You have quite an imagination!
> B: I didn't imagine it!
> C: What happened next, Junior!?
> B: My dad opened the door.
> C: What?
> B: Dad said, "Junior, why are you sitting on that pile of clothes I just washed? It looks like a mountain."
> B: Then he said, "You need to fold all of those clothes if you want pancakes."
> D: So, wait… the story is you had to fold some clothes before your dad made you pancakes?
> B: Yes—and it almost killed me.

## 236. A Difficult Person

> Vikram and Priti are enjoying a peaceful breakfast.
> Suddenly, a car horn beeps loudly outside their house.
> A: Who is making all of that noise so early in the morning?
> B: That must be Justin.
> A: Your old college roommate?
> B: Yes. I'm giving him a tour of the city today. He wants to buy a place here.
> A: You don't seem very excited.
> B: Well, Justin is a difficult person. He's very…
> The horn beeps four more times.
> A: Rude?
> Vikram goes outside and sees Justin in a shiny new car.
> Justin is wearing expensive designer clothes.
> C: Vikram! Wow. I forgot how small your house was! I keep telling you to get a bigger house, like mine!
> B: Yes, I know. You sent me photos of your house… and your cars… and your boat.
> C: Should we take your car or mine?
> B: I don't mind driving—
> Justin suddenly starts laughing.
> C: I'm joking! We're not going to take your old car! Mine is much nicer!
> Justin plays extremely loud music as they drive around town.
> B: Maybe you'd like to buy a place near the park?
> Justin turns down his music.
> C: Sorry! I couldn't hear you! The speakers in this new car are so loud!
> B: Never mind.
> B: Maybe you'll like downtown. That's where the clubs and restaurants are.
> Vikram and Justin drive downtown. They get out of the car and walk around.
> C: The restaurants in my city are much cooler than these.
> C: And the people are more fashionable.
> C: I really live in the best city in the world!
> B: Then why are you buying a place here?
> C: Because I don't have any friends there.

## 237. Pirate Land

> Zari and Lily are at an amusement park.
> A: Isn't Pirate Land the best?
> B: No.
> A: What do you want to do now? Go on the pirate ship? Visit the gift shop?
> B: I want to go home and sleep.
> A: We can't go until I find Paul. He works here. He got us these tickets to the park!
> B: Then let's find him quickly. This park is stupid. Real pirates never sang and danced together.
> A: Real pirates also never ate nachos, but you didn't complain when I bought you some.
> B: Yes, but they're delicious. Do you want some?
> Just then, Zari sees Paul.
> A: There he is! Isn't he cute in that pirate costume?
> B: He looks ridiculous. He has a parrot on his shoulder.
> A: Oh no. I'm terrified of parrots!
> B: You came here to talk to Paul. Just talk to him.
> Zari and Lily walk over to Paul.
> A: Hi, Paul!
> C: Hi, Zari! Wow, umm… it's great to see you!
> D: Squawk! Go away!
> Zari shouts and jumps back.
> C: I'm so sorry! Parrots don't understand what they're saying.
> A: Oh… OK.
> C: I wanted to tell you something, Zari.
> D: Squawk! You're ugly!
> A: I'm ugly?!
> C: No! That's the parrot talking! I think you look great!
> C: Zari, I wanted to ask you a question.
> A: Yes?
> Suddenly, the parrot flies off Paul's shoulder and lands in Lily's nachos.
> B: My nachos!
> A: Oh no! It's attacking us!
> Zari screams and runs away.
> C: Zari! Wait!
> A few minutes later, Lily finds Zari next to the pirate ship.
> B: That was hilarious.
> A: I'm so embarrassed. We have to leave now.
> B: No way, Pirate Land is great. And I need some more nachos.

## 238. I Can Predict the Future

> Bea and Lin are walking down the street.
> A: Do you want to go get a drink?
> B: I can't. I have to go home and finish a presentation for a client.
> A: No, you don't!
> B: Yes, I do, I have a meeting with this client tomorrow.
> A: Trust me, you don't have to worry about that meeting.
> B: How could you possibly know that?
> A: Well, because I can predict the future. I'm a psychic.
> B: Is that a joke?
> A: No! Seriously, I predict the future all the time.
> B: Prove it.
> A: You see that dog over there? He's going to stop and smell that tree.
> Lin points to a dog, who then smells a tree.
> B: That was easy! That's what all dog do.
> Just then, Bea gets a text.
> A: That's Joe. He wants to go on a date.
> Bea checks her phone and sees that Lin is right.
> B: Lucky guess. I told you yesterday that he likes me.
> A: Don't be jealous because you're not a psychic like me.
> B: Lin, look out!
> Suddenly a truck drives by, splashing Lin with water.
> A: Oh no! My clothes are soaked! We can't go to the bar now!
> B: Hahahaha! You said you can predict the future. Why didn't you know that was going to happen?
> A: Wow. Maybe I'm not a psychic…
> Just then, Bea gets a call from her boss. She looks really disappointed.
> A: Are you OK?
> B: No. My meeting tomorrow is canceled. That client just fired our company.
> A: Oh no! I'm sorry.
> B: I spent so much time on that presentation!
> A: Well, I did say that you had nothing to worry about…
> B: Maybe you can predict the future after all.

## 239. Uncle Edward's House

> Eddy and Junior walk into a big, dark house full of dusty, old furniture.
> A: Come on, Junior! I can't wait to show you this house.
> B: This house is scary!
> A: No, it's not. I came here a lot when I was little.
> A: Anyway, it's our house now! When Uncle Edward died, he left it to us.
> A: Although I always thought he hated me…
> B: Dad, are we moving here?
> A: Of course! It's much bigger than our apartment.
> B: But I love our apartment. This house looks dirty.
> A: It's just dark. Turn on the lights.
> Junior tries to turn on a light. Sparks come out of the wall.
> A: We'll fix that.
> They walk into a dining room with an enormous chandelier. Eddy touches it.
> A: I've always wanted a chandelier…
> B: Dad, look out!
> The chandelier falls and almost hits Eddy.
> A: Whoops. Wow, it's not broken!
> A: Hey, look at that amazing wallpaper.
> Junior looks closely at a wall covered in dark spots.
> B: That's mold.
> They go into a bedroom upstairs. There's a hole in the roof. Birds are flying in and out.
> B: We can't sleep here!
> A: You've always wanted a pet bird, right?
> Eddy and Junior walk into a bathroom.
> A: This is my favorite thing in the house!
> Eddy jumps into the bathtub.
> The floor breaks. Eddy and the bathtub fall down into the room below.
> Junior shouts down to Eddy.
> B: Dad! Are you OK?
> A: I'm fine!
> B: Dad, this house is really dangerous!
> A: Yeah. Now I know why Uncle Edward left it to me.
> Eddy and Junior drive home with the chandelier in their car.
> A: Well, at least we got a new chandelier.

## 240. Get Out!

> Lin and Lucy are walking down the street when it starts to rain.
> A: Let's go to a coffee shop to get out of the rain. How about this one?
> B: Oh, not that one.
> They continue walking.
> A: Oh, this one looks good!
> B: We can't go there either.
> A: What about the one next door?
> B: Definitely not.
> A: What's wrong with all these coffee shops?
> B: Well… I'm not allowed to go inside any of them.
> A: Are you serious? We're getting really wet.
> Frustrated, Lin walks into the closest coffee shop. Lucy follows her.
> C: Get out of here, Lucy!
> They quickly leave.
> B: He's mad because I illegally downloaded movies using the café's wifi connection.
> A: OK, let's go to the restaurant next door.
> They walk in, and the waiter bursts into tears.
> D: Lucy! How could you come here after you broke my heart?!
> B: Sorry, François. I've got to run!
> They rush out of the restaurant.
> A: What about this bakery?
> The owner at the bakery looks at Lucy angrily.
> B: Hi Ron…
> E: Get out!
> B: Sorry I took all your money in that poker game. We'll leave.
> A: You're making it impossible for us to get out of the rain in this neighborhood!
> B: Oh! There's a deli across the street.
> A: And you're still allowed in there?
> B: Yes! The owner loves me. I taught him all about cryptocurrency. He'll give us free coffee.
> A: Great!
> Later, after the rain stops, they walk to the park with their coffees.
> A: Why don't we sit there, next to the violin player?
> The violin player sees Lucy.
> F: Hey! I told you I never wanted to see you here again!
> A: What did you do to that guy?!
> B: Don't ask.

## 241. Late Fees

> Lily is standing at the librarian's desk in the library. She's trying to check out a book.
> A: I'm sorry, I can't let you check out this book. Your library card has been suspended.
> B: What?! My library card can't be suspended!
> The librarian points to a sign that says, "Quiet, please!"
> B: But I need this book for a school assignment.
> A: I'm sorry. You've checked out several books and you haven't returned them.
> B: What?! That's not possible.
> A: Shhh!
> The librarian points to the "Quiet, please!" sign again.
> A: It's a rule that I take very seriously.
> A: According to our records, you haven't returned "The History of Unicorns", "Teenage Vampires In Love, Volume One", and "Teenage Vampires In Love, Volume Two."
> B: I would never read any of those books. There must be something wrong with your computer.
> A: I'm sorry, but I can't let you check out another book until you return those books and then pay the late fees.
> B: Fine! I'll do my research on the Internet!
> Lily angrily walks away. Just then, she notices Zari in the library. She's reading volume two of "Teenage Vampires In Love."
> Lily grabs the book from Zari.
> B: Zari! Have you been checking out books with my library card?!
> C: I'm sorry! But you know how much I love reading!
> B: Why didn't you use your library card!?
> C: Because… they took it away. I always returned my books late, so I had a lot of late fees.
> B: Argh!
> C: Can you ever forgive me?
> B: Ahhh. I guess so.
> C: Great. Because I need you to check out "Teenage Vampires In Love, Volume Three"!

## 242. Painting at Sunrise

> Lin is painting in Oscar's studio.
> A: Ugh… My painting is boring.
> B: Well, sometimes you just need inspiration… and great light.
> Oscar points outside.
> B: There's an amazing view from the mountain. Go there at sunrise.
> A: Sunrise?! I hate waking up early!
> B: You have to. The light at sunrise is perfect.
> A: I hope the view is worth it.
> The next morning, Lin hikes up the mountain with her paint, canvas, and easel.
> She meets a hiker on the trail.
> C: Wow, that looks heavy! How far are you hiking?
> A: I'm going to the top of the mountain.
> C: That's three miles!
> A: What?!
> Two hours later, Lin arrives at the top and sets up her easel.
> A: Ugh, I'm exhausted. But the light here is perfect!
> As she picks up her paintbrush, a family sets up a picnic in front of her.
> A: Excuse me! I'm trying to paint.
> D: Oh, we'll only be here for a few minutes! Would you like a sandwich?
> A: No, thanks. I need to paint before the sunrise is over.
> Lin moves her easel to a new place. Just then, a bus full of tourists arrives.
> A: Hey! I'm trying to paint! Can you move?
> E: Sure, as soon as we get some pictures!
> The tourists all begin to take pictures.
> A: Ugh! The sunrise is gone!
> Lin angrily throws her brushes at the canvas.
> A: I quit!
> Lin hikes back down the mountain and returns to Oscar's studio.
> A: Here's your easel, Oscar.
> B: How did your painting go this morning?
> A: Not good.
> Lin shows Oscar the painting.
> B: You threw paint all over the canvas.
> A: Yes, I did.
> B: It's… magnificent! I love it!

## 243. A Relaxing Weekend

> Vikram's wife, Priti, has been working hard on a project for weeks.
> Vikram calls her at her office.
> A: Hi, Vikram! Am I late for lunch?
> B: It's actually dinner time.
> A: Oh, I didn't realize it was so late.
> B: You've been working so much that we haven't spent any time together…
> A: I know, I'm sorry.
> B: That's why I've planned a surprise weekend trip!
> A: Ah! That's just what I need.
> The next morning, Vikram drives Priti to the countryside.
> B: This isn't a regular hotel. It's a unique experience!
> They go to the front desk.
> C: Welcome, here are the keys to your barn.
> A: Barn?!
> B: We've never slept in a barn!
> A: Yes, because we're not horses.
> C: You'll love it! Would you like some water?
> A: That would be great!
> The receptionist hands Priti a bucket.
> C: The well is at the top of the hill.
> A: There's no faucet in the barn? I'm not walking up that hill.
> B: But the water will be so fresh!
> A: I'm too tired. I just want to go to sleep and wake up late tomorrow.
> The next day, a rooster wakes them up at five in the morning.
> The receptionist knocks on their door.
> C: Time to go! You don't want to be late.
> A: For what?
> C: For collecting eggs from our chickens to make breakfast!
> B: Ooh… you love fresh eggs, honey. Right?
> Next, Vikram and Priti have to milk a cow to get cream for coffee.
> A: Vikram, this is exhausting!
> B: I'm sorry. This is the opposite of a relaxing vacation.
> A: But on the other hand, I haven't thought about my stressful job in hours.
> B: So, should we stay another night?
> A: Absolutely not.

## 244. Nature Hike

> Zari and Lily are hiking through the forest. Lily keeps looking at her phone.
> A: Why did you bring your phone? We should enjoy nature.
> B: I'm not going into the woods without my phone. It's too dangerous.
> A: It's not dangerous. It's beautiful. Look around you!
> B: I only see danger.
> Lily takes a photo of a plant with her phone.
> B: My app says this plant is poisonous. Don't eat it.
> A: I'm not going to eat random plants, Lily.
> Lily and Zari keep walking.
> A: These trees are amazing.
> B: Falling trees kill over one hundred people every year.
> A: Look at these footprints! Cool!
> B: It might be a wolf…
> A: I'm pretty sure they're duck footprints.
> Lily takes a photo with her phone.
> B: The app says they're duck footprints.
> A: That's what I just said.
> Zari leads Lily up a hill.
> A: Look! There's a waterfall!
> Lily is still looking at the footprints on her phone. Zari turns around to look for Lily.
> A: Lily, you're missing everything!
> Without looking, Zari walks into a spider web.
> A: Ahh! I think there's a spider on my head!
> Zari jumps up and down and waves her arms.
> A: Help! Get this spider off me!
> Lily runs up to Zari with her phone.
> B: Stop moving, Zari! I'm trying to help!
> A: It might be poisonous! I'm going to die!
> Lily takes a photo of the spider, then brushes the spider off of Zari's head.
> B: Relax. The app says it's not poisonous.
> Lily shows Zari the picture of the spider on her phone.
> B: Look, that spider was beautiful!
> A: Oh, wow! I never even got to see it!
> B: Aren't you happy I brought my phone?
